(۶۵) یا یہ قول زمانہ سے زیادہ ہم آہنگ ہے۔ یا یہ قول دلیل میں واضح تر ہے۔ (٦٦ ) یہ اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ تصحیح میں تعارض ہو۔ یا تصحیح کی بالکل تصریح نہ ہو۔ (۱۷) پس لیے آپ اس قول کو جس کے لیے کوئی مریج ہو ۔ ان مرجحات میں سے جن کو آپ
جان چکے پس یہ نہایت واضح بات ہے۔ تصحیح کو ترجیح دینے کی دس صورتیں:
جب میں مختلف اقوال میں سے کسی ایک قول کی تصحیح کی علامتیں ( مخصوص ) بیان کر چکا اور یہ بھی بتا چکا کہ تصیح کے بعض الفاظ میں، بعض سے زیادہ تاکید ہے اور اس کا فائدہ تصحیح میں تعارض کے وقت ہی ظاہر ہوتا ہے اور تعارض کی صورت یہ ہے کہ صحیح کرنے والوں نے دونوں قولوں کی تصحیح کی ہو تو اب میں نے ان باتوں کو ان اشعار میں ایسی شاندار تفصیل سے پیش کیا ہے کہ مجھ سے پہلے کسی نے ایسا بیان نہیں کیا اور یہ تفصیل انہی مضامین سے ماخوذ ہے جن کو میں پہلے ممد کر
آیا ہوں۔
اور وہ تفصیل یہ ہے کہ فقہاء کا یہ قول کہ: " جب کسی مسئلہ میں دو قول تصحیح شدہ ہوں تو مفتی کو اختیار ہے“ یہ بات علی اطلاق ( ہر حال میں ) نہیں ہے بلکہ اس صورت میں ہے جب کسی قول کے لیے کوئی وجہ ترجیح موجود نہ ہو نہ صحیح سے پہلے نہ تصحیح کے بعد اور وجوہ ترجیح دس ہیں۔ جو
درج ذیل ہیں:
پہلی وجہ ترجیح
یہ ہے کہ ایک قول کی تصحیح لفظ صحیح سے ہو اور دوسرے کی لفظ اصح سے اور اس بارے میں گفتگو پہلے ہو چکی ہے اور یہ بات بھی گزر چکی ہے کہ : " مشہور قول اصبح کی صحیح پر ترجیح ہے۔" دوسری وجہ :
یہ ہے کہ ایک قول کی لفظ فتوی سے تصحیح کی گئی ہو اور دوسرے قول کی کسی اور لفظ سے جیسا
کہ اس کی تفصیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔
شرح رسم السلطنی
تیسری وجه یہ ہے کہ تصحیح شدہ دو قولوں میں سے ایک قول متون میں ہو اور دوسرا قول متوان کے علاوہ دیگر کتابوں میں ۔ کیونکہ کسی بھی قول کی تصحیح نہ ہونے کی صورت میں متن والے قول کو مقدم کیا جاتا ہے اس لیے کہ متون نقل مذہب کے لیے تصنیف کیے گئے ہیں۔ مضمون پہلے گزر چکا ہے۔ پس اس صورت میں بھی یہی حکم ہو گا جب دنوں تصحیحیں متعارض ہوں ۔ چنانچہ بحر باب قضاء الفوائت ( ج ۲ ص۸۶) میں ہے کہ : تصحیح اور فتوی میں اختلاف ہو گیا ہے اور اس قول پر جو متون کے موافق ہے عمل کرنا زیادہ بہتر ہے۔"
چوتھی وجہ : یہ ہے کہ ان میں سے ایک امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ کا قول ہو اور دوسرا آپ کے کسی شاگرد کا کیونکہ کسی بھی قول کی تصحیح نہ ہونے کی صورت میں امام صاحب کا قول مقدم ہوتا ہے۔ جس کی تفصیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔ پس تصحیح کے بعد بھی یہی حکم ہوگا۔
.
پانچویں وجہ : یہ ہے کہ ایک قول ظاہر روایت ہو تو اس کو دوسرے قول پر مقدم کیا جائے گا ۔ بحر کتاب الرضاع ( ج ۳ ص ۲۲۲) میں ہے کہ " جب فتوئی مختلف ہو تو ظاہر روایت کو ترجیح ہو گی اور باب المصرف ( ج ۲ ص ۲۵۰ ) میں ہے کہ : " جب تصحیح میں اختلاف ہو تو ظاہر روایت کی تفتیش کرنا اور اس کی طرف رجوع کرنا واجب ہے۔"
چھٹی وجہ :
یہ ہے کہ تصیح شدہ دوقولوں میں سے ایک کے قائل تمام بڑے مشائخ ہوں۔ کیونکہ اشباہ کی شرح بیری میں ہے کہ: " مشائخ سے جو طے شدہ بات مروی ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ جب کسی مسئلہ میں اختلاف ہو تو اس قول کا اعتبار ہوگا جس کے قائل اکثر حضرات ہیں اور اس طرح کی بات ہم پہلے حادی قدی کے حوالہ سے بھی بیان کر آئے ہیں۔
ساتویں وجہ :
یہ ہے کہ ایک قول استحسان ہو اور دوسرا قیات کیونکہ پہلے یہ بات آ چکی ہے کہ استحسان
...or all the great ones.
Sharh Rasm al-Mufti
(14) They are the proponents of this statement, or it is istihsan. Or it clearly increases benefit for endowments.
(65) Or this statement is more in harmony with the time. Or this statement is clearer in evidence. (66) This is in the case when there is conflict in tas'hih, or there is no explicit tas'hih at all. (17) So you choose the statement for which there is a weight (murajjih) among these weights that you have learned. So this is very clear. Ten scenarios for preferring a corrected opinion:
When I have mentioned the specific signs of tas'hih for one statement among various statements, and I have also explained that some words of tas'hih are more emphatic than others, and its benefit becomes apparent only at the time of conflict in tas'hih. And the form of conflict is that the correctors have declared both statements as sahih. Now I have presented these matters in verses with such splendid detail that no one before me has ever expressed such. And this detail is derived from the very topics that I have previously mentioned.
And that detail is that the jurists' statement: 'When two statements in a matter are muṣaḥḥaḥ, the mufti has a choice' — this is not absolute (in every case) but rather it applies only when there is no reason for preference (tarjih) for either statement, neither before tas'hih nor after tas'hih. And the reasons for preference are ten, as follows:
First reason for preference:
It is that one statement is corrected with the word 'sahih' and the other with the word 'asahh', and discussion about this has already passed. And it has also been stated that 'the well-known statement is given preference over asahh on sahih.'
Second reason:
It is that one statement is corrected with the word 'fatwa' and the other with some other word, as the detail has already passed.
Sharh Rasm al-Mufti
Third reason:
It is that of the two muṣaḥḥaḥ statements, one is in the mutun (core texts) and the other is in books other than the mutun. Because in the absence of any tas'hih of a statement, the statement of the mutun is given precedence, since the mutun were composed for transmitting the madhhab. This topic has already passed. So the same ruling will apply when both tas'hihs are conflicting. Accordingly, in al-Bahr, chapter of Qada al-Fawa'it (vol. 2, p. 86), it says: 'There is a difference between tas'hih and fatwa, and acting upon the statement that is in accordance with the mutun is better.'
Fourth reason:
It is that one of them is the statement of Imam A'zam (may Allah have mercy on him) and the other is the statement of one of his students. Because in the absence of any tas'hih of a statement, the Imam's statement is given precedence, the detail of which has already passed. So after tas'hih, the same ruling will apply.
Fifth reason:
It is that if one statement is ẓāhir al-riwāyah (widely transmitted), it will be given precedence over the other. In al-Bahr, chapter of Rada' (vol. 3, p. 222), it says: 'When fatwas differ, preference is given to ẓāhir al-riwāyah.' And in Bab al-Masrif (vol. 2, p. 250), it says: 'When there is a difference in tas'hih, it is obligatory to investigate and refer to ẓāhir al-riwāyah.'
Sixth reason:
It is that one of the two muṣaḥḥaḥ statements is held by all the great mashāyikh (senior scholars). Because in Sharh al-Ashbah by al-Birī it says: 'The settled matter narrated from the mashāyikh is that when there is a difference in a matter, the opinion of the majority is to be considered. And such a matter we have already mentioned with reference to Hādī Qudī [؟].'
Seventh reason:
It is that one statement is istihsan and the other is qiyas. Because it has already been mentioned that istihsan...
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Rasm al-Mufti discusses the methodology for a mufti when two corrected opinions (muṣaḥḥaḥ) on a matter exist and he must choose one. The author emphasizes that the general rule that the mufti has free choice is not absolute; it applies only when there is no reason to prefer one over the other. He then lists ten weighting factors (murajjihāt) for tas'hih. On the pages extracted, seven are detailed: 
1. Preference of 'asahh' over 'sahih' (the word indicating correction).
2. Preference of the opinion corrected with 'fatwa' over other correction terms.
3. Preference of the opinion found in the core texts (mutun) over those from other books.
4. Preference of the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa over his students.
5. Preference of the opinion that is ẓāhir al-riwāyah (from the well-known transmissions of Imam Muhammad).
6. Preference of the opinion held by the majority of senior scholars (mashāyikh).
7. Preference of istihsan over qiyas (the text cuts off here).
Each of these rules applies when there is a conflict between two corrected opinions, building upon similar principles that apply when there is no correction at all. The passage relies on earlier discussion in the same work and references like al-Bahr and Sharh al-Ashbah.

Key Terms
تصحیح (tas'hih): The process of declaring a particular ruling as the correct (sahih) position in the Hanafi madhhab, often by later scholars.
مرجحات (murajjihāt): Factors or criteria that tip the balance in favor of one opinion over another when both are considered valid.
ظاہر الروایۃ (zāhir al-riwāyah): Opinions transmitted in the six major works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, which form the most authoritative layer of the madhhab.
علی اطلاق (ʿalā al-itlāq): Absolutely, without restriction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a mufti free to choose between two muṣaḥḥaḥ opinions?
A) Always, because both are sahih.
B) Only after seeking guidance from a senior scholar.
C) Only when there is no reason for preference (tarjih) for either.
D) Only when the opinions are from different generations.

Key Takeaway
A mufti's freedom to choose between two muṣaḥḥaḥ opinions is conditional on the absence of any tarjih factor; the ten murajjihāt must be checked first.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
The First Three Murajjihāt for Corrected Opinions
Listing and explaining the first three weighting factors for preferred corrected opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the first three murajjihāt (weighting factors) from the ten: quality of tas'hih word, use of 'fatwa', and presence in the mutun.

Core Idea
When two corrected opinions conflict, prefer the one with stronger tas'hih wording, marked with 'fatwa', or found in the core texts.

The passage enumerates ten factors to prefer one corrected opinion over another. This lesson focuses on the first three, which are based on the language of tas'hih, the term 'fatwa', and the source book type. These factors help a mufti make a systematic, non-arbitrary choice when earlier scholars have not explicitly settled the matter.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first murajjih: the wording of tas'hih
If one opinion is corrected with 'asahh' (most correct) and the other with 'sahih' (correct), the one with 'asahh' is preferred. The text says 'المشہور قول اصح کی صحیح پر ترجیح ہے'.
The comparison is between 'sahih' and 'asahh'; note that 'asahh' indicates a higher degree of correctness.
2
Apply the second murajjih: the word 'fatwa'
If one opinion is explicitly marked as 'the fatwa' (i.e., the operative ruling), it is preferred over an opinion corrected with a different term. The passage states this as the second reason.
3
Apply the third murajjih: the source book type
An opinion found in the mutun (core texts of the madhhab) is preferred over one from other books, because the mutun were composed specifically to transmit the madhhab. The passage cites al-Bahr to support this.
Even in the absence of tas'hih, the mutun opinion is preferred; the same holds after tas'hih.
4
Analyse a scenario with conflicting murajjihāt
Suppose one opinion is corrected with 'asahh' but is from a non-mutun book, while another is corrected with 'sahih' but from a mutun. Which prevails? The passage does not rank them, but later Hanafi works provide a hierarchy; for this lesson, note that both factors are valid and further investigation is needed.
Real tarjih often requires considering multiple factors and sometimes consulting a superior scholar.

And that detail is that the jurists' statement: 'When two statements in a matter are muṣaḥḥaḥ, the mufti has a choice' — this is not absolute (in every case) but rather it applies only when there is no reason for preference (tarjih) for either statement, neither before tas'hih nor after tas'hih. And the reasons for preference are ten, as follows:
First reason for preference:
It is that one statement is corrected with the word 'sahih' and the other with the word 'asahh', and discussion about this has already passed. And it has also been stated that 'the well-known statement is given preference over asahh on sahih.'
Second reason:
It is that one statement is corrected with the word 'fatwa' and the other with some other word, as the detail has already passed.
Sharh Rasm al-Mufti
Third reason:
It is that of the two muṣaḥḥaḥ statements, one is in the mutun (core texts) and the other is in books other than the mutun. Because in the absence of any tas'hih of a statement, the statement of the mutun is given precedence, since the mutun were composed for transmitting the madhhab. This topic has already passed. So the same ruling will apply when both tas'hihs are conflicting. Accordingly, in al-Bahr, chapter of Qada al-Fawa'it (vol. 2, p. 86), it says: 'There is a difference between tas'hih and fatwa, and acting upon the statement that is in accordance with the mutun is better.'
Fourth reason:
It is that one of them is the statement of Imam A'zam (may Allah have mercy on him) and the other is the statement of one of his students. Because in the absence of any tas'hih of a statement, the Imam's statement is given precedence, the detail of which has already passed. So after tas'hih, the same ruling will apply.
Fifth reason:
It is that if one statement is ẓāhir al-riwāyah (widely transmitted), it will be given precedence over the other. In al-Bahr, chapter of Rada' (vol. 3, p. 222), it says: 'When fatwas differ, preference is given to ẓāhir al-riwāyah.' And in Bab al-Masrif (vol. 2, p. 250), it says: 'When there is a difference in tas'hih, it is obligatory to investigate and refer to ẓāhir al-riwāyah.'
Sixth reason:
It is that one of the two muṣaḥḥaḥ statements is held by all the great mashāyikh (senior scholars). Because in Sharh al-Ashbah by al-Birī it says: 'The settled matter narrated from the mashāyikh is that when there is a difference in a matter, the opinion of the majority is to be considered. And such a matter we have already mentioned with reference to Hādī Qudī [؟].'
Seventh reason:
It is that one statement is istihsan and the other is qiyas. Because it has already been mentioned that istihsan...
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Rasm al-Mufti discusses the methodology for a mufti when two corrected opinions (muṣaḥḥaḥ) on a matter exist and he must choose one. The author emphasizes that the general rule that the mufti has free choice is not absolute; it applies only when there is no reason to prefer one over the other. He then lists ten weighting factors (murajjihāt) for tas'hih. On the pages extracted, seven are detailed: 
1. Preference of 'asahh' over 'sahih' (the word indicating correction).
2. Preference of the opinion corrected with 'fatwa' over other correction terms.
3. Preference of the opinion found in the core texts (mutun) over those from other books.
4. Preference of the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa over his students.
5. Preference of the opinion that is ẓāhir al-riwāyah (from the well-known transmissions of Imam Muhammad).
6. Preference of the opinion held by the majority of senior scholars (mashāyikh).
7. Preference of istihsan over qiyas (the text cuts off here).
Each of these rules applies when there is a conflict between two corrected opinions, building upon similar principles that apply when there is no correction at all. The passage relies on earlier discussion in the same work and references like al-Bahr and Sharh al-Ashbah.

Key Terms
اصح (asahh): A term used in tas'hih meaning 'most correct', indicating a higher degree of correctness than 'sahih'.
فتوی (fatwa): The operational ruling given for practice; used as a tas'hih term to indicate the relied-upon opinion.
متون (mutun): The core authoritative texts of the Hanafi madhhab, such as al-Hidāyah, al-Qudūrī, and al-Mukhtār.
بحر (al-Bahr): Al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq, a major Hanafi fiqh commentary by Ibn Nujaym.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first murajjih, which corrected opinion is preferred?
A) The one corrected with 'sahih'.
B) The one corrected with 'asahh'.
C) Neither, they are equal.
D) The one corrected with 'fatwa'.

Key Takeaway
The first three murajjihāt—quality of tas'hih word, use of 'fatwa', and occurrence in mutun—provide a systematic method for preferring one corrected opinion over another.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Tarjih Based on Textual Hierarchy: Matn, Imam, and Zahir al-Riwayah
Lists grounds 3–5 for tarjih among corrected opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the first three grounds of tarjih (matn, imam, zahir al-riwayah) to resolve a conflict between two corrected opinions in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
When corrected opinions conflict, prefer the one in the matn, then the Imam's, then Zahir al-Riwayah.

When two tashihs conflict, a mufti cannot choose arbitrarily. The Hanafi school provides a clear hierarchy based on textual authority. The first three grounds relate to the source of the opinion: Is it in the core matn texts? Is it from Imam Abu Hanifa or his students? Does it belong to Zahir al-Riwayah? Understanding this hierarchy ensures the mufti gives precedence to the most authoritative transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify conflicting corrected opinions
First, confirm that both opinions have been subject to tashih by later scholars but they lead to different rulings. Determine which opinion is found in the mutun (core texts like al-Quduri or al-Hidayah).
Mutun are composed specifically to transmit the relied-upon positions.
2
Check authorship: Imam vs. student
If one opinion is from Imam Abu Hanifa and the other from his students (Abu Yusuf or Muhammad), the Imam's opinion takes precedence unless the tashih explicitly indicates otherwise.
This applies even after tashih, as the Imam's authority remains higher.
3
Verify Zahir al-Riwayah
If the opinions are from different transmission levels, the one from Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Muhammad al-Shaybani) is preferred. This is the most authoritative layer of the madhhab.
Al-Bahr states it is obligatory to investigate Zahir al-Riwayah when tashih conflicts.
4
Apply the hierarchy
Apply these three grounds sequentially. The first ground that clearly differentiates the opinions determines the mufta bihi. If matn status is equal, move to the Imam's view; if still equal, check Zahir al-Riwayah.
These grounds are only applicable when both opinions are corrected.

How do you give a fatwa? Its detail has passed before. Explanation of Rasm al-Mufti: The third reason is that among the two corrected opinions, one is in the matn (core texts) and the other is in books other than the matn. Because when there is no correction of any opinion, the opinion in the matn is given precedence because the matn were composed for transmitting the madhhab. This topic has passed before. So in this case too, the same ruling applies when the two corrections are conflicting. Scholars have clarified in Hadi Qady and other books that in issues where scholars differ, the fatwa is given on the opinion that brings more benefit to the waqf. The ninth reason is that one of them is more suitable for the time. Because the opinion that agrees with people's custom or brings more ease for them is more reliable, and for this reason scholars have given fatwa on the opinion of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). (1) Regarding the issue of tazkiyah (verification) of witnesses being necessary and not deciding on apparent justice, because the conditions of time changed. Since Imam al-A'zam (may Allah have mercy on him) was in a century for which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) testified to its goodness, and the time of the Sahibayn was different. Because in their time, lying had spread among people, so tazkiyah of witnesses became necessary in their time. (2) Similarly, scholars deviated from the opinion of our three Imams regarding the issue of the permissibility of ijarah (hire) for teaching, etc. Because time changed and the need for a fatwa of permissibility arose. Its detail has passed before. The tenth reason is that one opinion has a clear and strong new evidence. Because it has already been stated that preference is also attained by the strength of evidence. Therefore, where two corrections are found and one who has the ability to reflect on evidence sees that the evidence for one opinion is stronger, acting on it is better. Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is from Rasm al-Mufti literature, specifically from 'Sharh Rasm al-Mufti'. The author lists nine grounds (starting from the third) for preferring one corrected opinion over another when two opinions are both corrected and conflicting. The first two grounds were presumably covered earlier. The grounds are as follows:

(3) Textual Authority: If one corrected opinion is found in the mutun (core texts like Mukhtasar al-Quduri or al-Hidayah) and the other is from non-mutun works, the matn opinion is preferred. This is because the mutun were specifically written to transmit the relied-upon positions of the madhhab. The author cites al-Bahr as evidence.

(4) Imam vs. Student: If one opinion is from Abu Hanifa and the other from his students (Abu Yusuf or Muhammad), the Imam's opinion is preferred, even after correction, unless the correction indicates otherwise.

(5) Zahir al-Riwayah: Opinions reported in the six core books of Muhammad al-Shaybani (Zahir al-Riwayah) are preferred over others. The author quotes al-Bahr to emphasize that investigating and referring to Zahir al-Riwayah is obligatory when tashih conflicts.

(6) Majority of Mashayikh: If one opinion is upheld by the majority of the great later scholars (mashayikh), that opinion is preferred. This is based on the principle that the view of the majority is given weight.

(7) Istihsan over Qiyas: If one opinion is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and the other on strict qiyas (analogy), the istihsan opinion is preferred, except in a few exceptional issues. This is a well-known principle in Hanafi usul.

(8) Benefit for Waqf: If one opinion is more beneficial for endowment (waqf) purposes, it is preferred. Scholars like al-Hadi al-Qady have explicitly stated this.

(9) Suitability for the Time/Custom: The opinion that aligns with contemporary custom (urf) or provides greater ease (taysir) is preferred. The author gives two examples: (a) The requirement of tazkiyah (background check) for witnesses changed from Imam Abu Hanifa's time (when people were trustworthy) to the Sahibayn's time (when lying spread), so the Sahibayn's opinion requiring tazkiyah became the fatwa. (b) The permissibility of ijarah for teaching etc. – despite the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) ruling it invalid, later scholars adopted the opinion of permissibility due to changing times and necessity.

(10) Strength of Evidence: The opinion with the stronger dalil (evidence) is preferred. This requires the mufti to have the ability to weigh evidence.

Finally, the author notes that these grounds apply in two scenarios: (1) when there is a conflict in tashih (i.e., both opinions have been corrected by later scholars but in contradictory ways), and (2) presumably another scenario (but the text cuts off). The passage ends mid-sentence. The student should understand that a mufti does not simply pick any corrected opinion; he must apply a hierarchy of preference based on authority, transmission, majority, istihsan, benefit, custom, and strength of evidence.

Key Terms
تصحیح (tashih): The process of determining and endorsing the correct or relied-upon opinion within the Hanafi school by later scholars.
تعارض (ta'arud): Conflict or contradiction between two tashīhāt (corrected opinions) where each opinion has been endorsed by different scholars or in different sources.
ترجیح (tarjih): The process of preferring one opinion over another based on certain criteria when both are considered corrected.
ظاہر روایت (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani containing the most authoritative and widely transmitted rulings of Abu Hanifa and his students.
متون (mutun): The core summarized texts of the Hanafi school, such as Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Hidayah, etc., which were composed to transmit the relied-upon positions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is given precedence when there is a conflict in tashih and one opinion is from Zahir al-Riwayah while the other is not?
A) The opinion from Zahir al-Riwayah is preferred.
B) The other opinion is preferred because later authors corrected it.
C) The mufti chooses whichever opinion is easier for the people.
D) The opinion from the Imam's student is preferred.

Key Takeaway
When corrected opinions conflict, first check matn, then Imam vs student, then Zahir al-Riwayah in that order.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Contextual Tarjih: Majority, Istihsan, Waqf, Custom, and Evidence
Lists grounds 6–10 for tarjih among corrected opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply grounds 6-10 of tarjih (majority, istihsan, waqf benefit, custom, and evidence strength) to resolve conflicts between corrected opinions in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
When textual hierarchy fails, prefer the opinion supported by majority, istihsan, waqf benefit, custom, or stronger evidence.

The Hanafi school does not rely solely on textual authority for tarjih. When grounds 3-5 are exhausted, the mufti turns to contextual considerations. These include the consensus of the great mashayikh, the preference of istihsan over qiyas, the benefit of waqf, suitability for the time and custom, and the strength of evidence. These grounds allow the madhhab to remain practical and responsive to changing circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Verify majority support among mashayikh
Check if one opinion is upheld by the majority of the great later scholars (mashayikh). If so, that opinion is preferred. This is based on the principle that the view of the majority carries weight.
Refer to Sharh al-Ashbah and Hadi Qady for such transmissions.
2
Identify if one opinion is based on istihsan
If one corrected opinion is derived via istihsan and the other via strict qiyas, the istihsan-based opinion is preferred, except in a few exceptional issues.
Istihsan is a recognized source in Hanafi usul, giving flexibility.
3
Check benefit for waqf
In matters related to waqf (endowments), the opinion that brings more benefit to the waqf is preferred. This is explicitly stated by scholars like al-Hadi al-Qady.
This ground is specific to waqf issues.
4
Assess suitability for time and custom
If one opinion aligns better with current custom (urf) or provides greater ease (taysir), it is preferred. Examples include tazkiyah of witnesses and ijarah for teaching.
Changes in social conditions justify adopting the Sahibayn's view over the Imam's.
5
Evaluate strength of evidence (dalil)
If the mufti has the capacity, he may compare the strength of evidence (dalil) for each opinion. The opinion with the stronger, clearer evidence is preferred.
This requires jtihad ability; not all muftis can perform this.

آپ فتوی کیسے دیں؟ کہ اس کی تفصیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔
شرح رسم المفتي تیسری وجه یہ ہے کہ تصحیح شدہ دو قولوں میں سے ایک قول متون میں ہو اور دوسرا قول متوان کے علاوہ دیگر کتابوں میں ۔ کیونکہ کسی بھی قول کی تصحیح نہ ہونے کی صورت میں متن والے قول کو مقدم کیا جاتا ہے اس لیے کہ متون نقل مذہب کے لیے تصنیف کیے گئے ہیں۔ مضمون پہلے گزر چکا ہے۔ پس اس صورت میں بھی یہی حکم ہو گا جب دنوں تصحیحیں متعارض ہوں ۔ چنانچہ بحر باب قضاء الفوائت ( ج ۲ ص۸۶) میں ہے کہ : تصحیح اور فتوی میں اختلاف ہو گیا ہے اور اس قول پر جو متون کے موافق ہے عمل کرنا زیادہ بہتر ہے۔" چوتھی وجہ : یہ ہے کہ ان میں سے ایک امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ کا قول ہو اور دوسرا آپ کے کسی شاگرد کا کیونکہ کسی بھی قول کی تصحیح نہ ہونے کی صورت میں امام صاحب کا قول مقدم ہوتا ہے۔ جس کی تفصیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔ پس تصحیح کے بعد بھی یہی حکم ہوگا۔
پانچویں وجہ : یہ ہے کہ ایک قول ظاہر روایت ہو تو اس کو دوسرے قول پر مقدم کیا جائے گا ۔ بحر کتاب الرضاع ( ج ۳ ص ۲۲۲) میں ہے کہ " جب فتوئی مختلف ہو تو ظاہر روایت کو ترجیح ہو گی اور باب المصرف ( ج ۲ ص ۲۵۰ ) میں ہے کہ : " جب تصحیح میں اختلاف ہو تو ظاہر روایت کی تفتیش کرنا اور اس کی طرف رجوع کرنا واجب ہے۔"
چھٹی وجہ : یہ ہے کہ تصیح شدہ دوقولوں میں سے ایک کے قائل تمام بڑے مشائخ ہوں۔ کیونکہ اشباہ کی شرح بیری میں ہے کہ: " مشائخ سے جو طے شدہ بات مروی ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ جب کسی مسئلہ میں اختلاف ہو تو اس قول کا اعتبار ہوگا جس کے قائل اکثر حضرات ہیں اور اس طرح کی بات ہم پہلے حادی قدی کے حوالہ سے بھی بیان کر آئے ہیں۔
ساتویں وجہ : یہ ہے کہ ایک قول استحسان ہو اور دوسرا قیات کیونکہ پہلے یہ بات آ چکی ہے کہ استحسان آپ فتوی کیسے دیں؟ ارج ہے مگر چند مسائل میں ۔
ٹھویں وجہ : یہ ہے کہ ایک قول وقف کے حق میں زیادہ مفید ہو۔ علماء نے حادی قدسی وغیرہ کتابوں میں اس وجہ ترجیح کی صراحت کی ہے کہ جن مسائل میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے ان میں فتویٰ اس قول پر دیا جائے گا جس میں وقف کا زیادہ نفع ہو۔
نویس وجہ : یہ ہے کہ ان میں سے ایک قول زمانہ کے لیے زیادہ مناسب ہے۔ کیونکہ جو قول لوگوں کے عرف کے موافق ہے یا اس میں لوگوں کے لیے زیادہ آسانی ہے وہ زیادہ قابل اعتماد ہے اور اس وجہ سے علماء نے صاحبین کے قول پر فتوی دیا ہے۔ (1) گواہوں کا تزکیہ ضروری ہونے کے مسئلہ میں اور ظاہری عدالت پر فیصلہ نہ کرنے کے بارے میں زمانہ کے احوال بدل جانے کی وجہ سے کیونکہ امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ اس قرن میں تھے۔ جس کے لیے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بہتری کی گواہی دی ہے اور صاحبین کا زمانہ اس سے مختلف تھا۔ کیونکہ ان کے زمانہ میں لوگوں میں جھوٹ پھیل چکا تھا اس لیے ان کے زمانہ میں گواہوں کا تزکیہ مضروری ہو گیا تھا۔ (۲) اسی طرح علماء نے تعلیم وغیرہ پر اجارہ جائز نہ ہونے کے سلسلہ میں ہمارے تینوں ائمہ کے قول سے عدول کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ زمانہ بدل گیا اور جواز کے فتویٰ کی ضرورت پیش آئی۔ جس کی تفصیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔
دسویں وجہ : یہ ہے کہ ایک قول نئی دلیل زیادہ واضح اور خوب ظاہر ہو۔ کیونکہ پہلے یہ بات بیان کی جا چکی ہے کہ دلیل کی قوت کی وجہ سے بھی ترجیح حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا جہاں دو تصحیحیں پائی جاتی ہوں اور وہ شخص جو دلیل میں غور و فکر کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے دیکھے کہ ان میں سے ایک قول کی دلیل زیادہ قوی ہے تو اس پر عمل کرنا زیادہ بہتر ہے۔
مذکورہ بالا وجوه ترجیح درج ذیل دو صورتوں میں ہیں۔ (1) جب تصحیح میں تعارض ہو کیونکہ اس صورت میں دونوں قولوں میں سے ہر ایک قول I
How do you give a fatwa? Its detail has passed before. Explanation of Rasm al-Mufti: The third reason is that among the two corrected opinions, one is in the matn (core texts) and the other is in books other than the matn. Because when there is no correction of any opinion, the opinion in the matn is given precedence because the matn were composed for transmitting the madhhab. This topic has passed before. So in this case too, the same ruling applies when the two corrections are conflicting. Thus in al-Bahr, chapter Qada al-Fawa'it (vol. 2, p. 86): 'There is a difference between tashih and fatwa, and acting upon the opinion that agrees with the matn is better.' The fourth reason is that one of them is the opinion of Imam al-A'zam (may Allah have mercy on him) and the other is the opinion of one of his students, because when there is no correction of any opinion, the opinion of Imam is given precedence. Its detail has passed before. So after correction, the same ruling applies. The fifth reason is that if one opinion is from Zahir al-Riwayah, it is given precedence over the other. In al-Bahr, kitab al-Rada' (vol. 3, p. 222): 'When fatwas differ, Zahir al-Riwayah is given preference.' And in Bab al-Masraf (vol. 2, p. 250): 'When there is a difference in tashih, it is obligatory to investigate Zahir al-Riwayah and refer to it.' The sixth reason is that one of the two corrected opinions is held by all the great mashayikh. Because in Sharh al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir: 'It is transmitted from the mashayikh that when there is a difference in a matter, the opinion held by the majority is relied upon.' And we have mentioned this before with reference to Hadi Qady. The seventh reason is that one opinion is istihsan and the other is qiyas, because it has already been stated that istihsan is preferred except in a few issues. How do you give a fatwa? It is preferable except in a few issues. The eighth reason is that one opinion is more beneficial for the waqf (endowment). Scholars have clarified in Hadi Qady and other books that in issues where scholars differ, the fatwa is given on the opinion that brings more benefit to the waqf. The ninth reason is that one of them is more suitable for the time. Because the opinion that agrees with people's custom or brings more ease for them is more reliable, and for this reason scholars have given fatwa on the opinion of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). (1) Regarding the issue of tazkiyah (verification) of witnesses being necessary and not deciding on apparent justice, because the conditions of time changed. Since Imam al-A'zam (may Allah have mercy on him) was in a century for which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) testified to its goodness, and the time of the Sahibayn was different. Because in their time, lying had spread among people, so tazkiyah of witnesses became necessary in their time. (2) Similarly, scholars deviated from the opinion of our three Imams regarding the issue of the permissibility of ijarah (hire) for teaching, etc. Because time changed and the need for a fatwa of permissibility arose. Its detail has passed before. The tenth reason is that one opinion has a clear and strong new evidence. Because it has already been stated that preference is also attained by the strength of evidence. Therefore, where two corrections are found and one who has the ability to reflect on evidence sees that the evidence for one opinion is stronger, acting on it is better. The aforementioned grounds of preference apply in the following two situations: (1) When there is a conflict in tashih, because in this case each of the two opinions... I
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is from Rasm al-Mufti literature, specifically from 'Sharh Rasm al-Mufti'. The author lists nine grounds (starting from the third) for preferring one corrected opinion over another when two opinions are both corrected and conflicting. The first two grounds were presumably covered earlier. The grounds are as follows:

(3) Textual Authority: If one corrected opinion is found in the mutun (core texts like Mukhtasar al-Quduri or al-Hidayah) and the other is from non-mutun works, the matn opinion is preferred. This is because the mutun were specifically written to transmit the relied-upon positions of the madhhab. The author cites al-Bahr as evidence.

(4) Imam vs. Student: If one opinion is from Abu Hanifa and the other from his students (Abu Yusuf or Muhammad), the Imam's opinion is preferred, even after correction, unless the correction indicates otherwise.

(5) Zahir al-Riwayah: Opinions reported in the six core books of Muhammad al-Shaybani (Zahir al-Riwayah) are preferred over others. The author quotes al-Bahr to emphasize that investigating and referring to Zahir al-Riwayah is obligatory when tashih conflicts.

(6) Majority of Mashayikh: If one opinion is upheld by the majority of the great later scholars (mashayikh), that opinion is preferred. This is based on the principle that the view of the majority is given weight.

(7) Istihsan over Qiyas: If one opinion is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and the other on strict qiyas (analogy), the istihsan opinion is preferred, except in a few exceptional issues. This is a well-known principle in Hanafi usul.

(8) Benefit for Waqf: If one opinion is more beneficial for endowment (waqf) purposes, it is preferred. Scholars like al-Hadi al-Qady have explicitly stated this.

(9) Suitability for the Time/Custom: The opinion that aligns with contemporary custom (urf) or provides greater ease (taysir) is preferred. The author gives two examples: (a) The requirement of tazkiyah (background check) for witnesses changed from Imam Abu Hanifa's time (when people were trustworthy) to the Sahibayn's time (when lying spread), so the Sahibayn's opinion requiring tazkiyah became the fatwa. (b) The permissibility of ijarah for teaching etc. – despite the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) ruling it invalid, later scholars adopted the opinion of permissibility due to changing times and necessity.

(10) Strength of Evidence: The opinion with the stronger dalil (evidence) is preferred. This requires the mufti to have the ability to weigh evidence.

Finally, the author notes that these grounds apply in two scenarios: (1) when there is a conflict in tashih (i.e., both opinions have been corrected by later scholars but in contradictory ways), and (2) presumably another scenario (but the text cuts off). The passage ends mid-sentence. The student should understand that a mufti does not simply pick any corrected opinion; he must apply a hierarchy of preference based on authority, transmission, majority, istihsan, benefit, custom, and strength of evidence.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that deviates from strict qiyas due to a stronger evidence, necessity, or custom.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical deduction from a revealed text to a new case based on a common effective cause ('illah).
وقف (waqf): An endowment of property for charitable purposes, with the corpus preserved and the usufruct dedicated to beneficiaries.
عرف (urf): Custom or common practice that is recognized as a source of law when not contradicting revealed texts.
دلیل (dalil): Evidence or proof from the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or Qiyas that supports a legal ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which ground justifies preferring the Sahibayn's opinion on tazkiyah of witnesses over Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion?
A) Majority of mashayikh
B) Istihsan over qiyas
C) Suitability for time/custom
D) Strength of evidence

Key Takeaway
When textual hierarchy does not resolve the conflict, turn to contextual grounds: majority, istihsan, waqf benefit, custom, and evidence strength, applied with consideration of changed circumstances.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Reasons for Preference Among Conflicting Rulings
Listing reasons for tarjeeh in Hanafi fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the reasons for preferring one Hanafi ruling over another when issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti prefers the opinion that is more beneficial, suitable for the time, or backed by stronger evidence.

This passage from a rasm al-mufti manual outlines the criteria a Hanafi mufti uses to choose between conflicting scholarly opinions. It explains that preference is not arbitrary but follows established principles such as benefit for waqf, suitability for the time, and strength of evidence. Understanding these reasons is crucial for issuing fatwas that are both authentic and relevant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the explicit reasons (wujuh al-tarjeeh)
Locate the four reasons mentioned: 1) more beneficial for waqf, 2) more suitable for the time, 3) stronger evidence (dalil aqwa), 4) a new evidence that clarifies the ruling. Note that the first reason is specific to endowment issues, while the others are general.
The passage also references that the opinion being in authoritative texts, from Imam Abu Hanifa, or from Zahir al-Riwayah are additional preferential factors.
2
Analyze the application of taghayyur al-zaman (change of time)
Examine the example of witness tazkiyah: Imam Abu Hanifa did not require it because of general trustworthiness, but later scholars (Sahibayn) made it necessary due to the spread of lying. Recognize that custom ('urf) and societal changes shift the preferred ruling.
This principle is also illustrated by the permissibility of ijarah for teaching, which classical Hanafi scholars prohibited but later allowed due to necessity.
3
Understand the role of evidence strength (qiwat al-dalil)
When two opinions exist and a qualified scholar determines one has stronger evidence, that opinion should be preferred. This is a universal tarjeeh criterion based on the quality of the proof.
The text emphasizes that this requires the ability to critically evaluate evidence (tamayyuz al-dalil).
4
Distinguish the two situations where tarjeeh is applied
First, when both opinions are equally correct (conflict in tashih), any additional strength tips the balance. Second, when neither opinion has been explicitly deemed correct, preference is given to the one with any of the listed factors (e.g., being in authoritative texts, from Imam Abu Hanifa, or from Zahir al-Riwayah).
The mufti must first assess whether the conflict is within the primary or secondary level of the school's literature.

شروع رسم الملتـی
یہ ہے کہ ایک قول وقف کے حق میں زیادہ مفید ہو۔ علماء نے حادی قدسی وغیرہ کتابوں میں اس وجہ ترجیح کی صراحت کی ہے کہ جن مسائل میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے ان میں فتویٰ اس قول پر دیا جائے گا جس میں وقف کا زیادہ نفع ہو۔
پنجم وجہ : یہ ہے کہ ان میں سے ایک قول زمانہ کے لیے زیادہ مناسب ہے۔ کیونکہ جو قول لوگوں کے عرف کے موافق ہے یا اس میں لوگوں کے لیے زیادہ آسانی ہے وہ زیادہ قابل اعتماد ہے اور اس وجہ سے علماء نے صاحبین کے قول پر فتوی دیا ہے۔ (1) گواہوں کا تزکیہ ضروری ہونے کے مسئلہ میں اور ظاہری عدالت پر فیصلہ نہ کرنے کے بارے میں زمانہ کے احوال بدل جانے کی وجہ سے کیونکہ امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ اس قرن میں تھے۔ جس کے لیے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بہتری کی گواہی دی ہے اور صاحبین کا زمانہ اس سے مختلف تھا۔ کیونکہ ان کے زمانہ میں لوگوں میں جھوٹ پھیل چکا تھا اس لیے ان کے زمانہ میں گواہوں کا تزکیہ ضروری ہو گیا تھا۔ (۲) اسی طرح علماء نے تعلیم وغیرہ پر اجارہ جائز نہ ہونے کے سلسلہ میں ہمارے تینوں ائمہ کے قول سے عدول کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ زمانہ بدل گیا اور جواز کے فتویٰ کی ضرورت پیش آئی۔ جس کی تفصیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔
دسویں وجہ : یہ ہے کہ ایک قول نئی دلیل زیادہ واضح اور خوب ظاہر ہو۔ کیونکہ پہلے یہ بات بیان کی جا چکی ہے کہ دلیل کی قوت کی وجہ سے بھی ترجیح حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا جہاں دو تصحیحیں پائی جاتی ہوں اور وہ شخص جو دلیل میں غور و فکر کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے دیکھے کہ ان میں سے ایک قول کی دلیل زیادہ قوی ہے تو اس پر عمل کرنا زیادہ بہتر ہے۔
مذکورہ بالا وجوه ترجیح درج ذیل دو صورتوں میں ہیں۔ (1) جب تصحیح میں تعارض ہو کیونکہ اس صورت میں دونوں قولوں میں سے ہر ایک قول صحت میں دوسرے قول کے ہم پلہ ہو گا اس لیے جب ان میں سے کسی ایک قول میں کسی اور جہت سے زیادہ قوت پیدا ہوگی تو اس قول پر بہ نسبت دوسرے قول کے عمل کرنا زیادہ بہتر ہوگا۔
(۲) اسی طرح جب دو قولوں میں سے کسی بھی قول کی صراحت تصحیح نہ کی گئی ہو تو اس قول کو مقدم کیا جائے گا جس میں مذکورہ بالا وجوہ ترجیح میں سے کوئی وجہ پائی جاتی ہو مثال اس قول کا متون میں ہونا یا امام اعظم کا قول ہونا یا ظاہر روایت ہونا الی آخرہ۔
Start of Rasm al-Mufti: This is that one statement is more beneficial for the endowment. The scholars have specified in books like Hadi Qudsi etc. this reason for preference: that in those issues where scholars differ, the fatwa will be given on that statement in which there is more benefit for the endowment. Fifth reason: This is that among them one statement is more suitable for the time. Because whatever statement is in accordance with the custom of the people or in which there is more ease for the people, it is more reliable, and for this reason the scholars gave fatwa on the statement of the two companions (Sahibayn). (1) In the issue of the necessity of tazkiyah of witnesses and not judging on apparent integrity due to changing circumstances of the time, because Imam A'zam (may Allah have mercy on him) was in that century for which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) testified goodness, and the time of the Sahibayn was different from that. Because in their time, lying had spread among people, so in their time, tazkiyah of witnesses became necessary. (2) Similarly, the scholars departed from the statement of our three imams regarding the impermissibility of ijarah for teaching etc., because the time changed and the need for a fatwa of permissibility arose, the details of which have passed earlier. Tenth reason: This is that one statement may become clearer and more manifest due to a new evidence. Because it has been previously stated that preference is also achieved due to strength of evidence. Therefore, when two tashihs are found, and the person who has the ability to ponder and reflect on evidence sees that the evidence of one of the statements is stronger, then acting upon it is better. The aforementioned reasons for preference exist in the following two situations: (1) When there is conflict in tashih, because in that case each of the two statements is equal to the other in correctness. So when any of these statements gains more strength from another direction, then acting upon that statement is better compared to the other. (2) Similarly, when neither of the two statements has been explicitly deemed correct, then that statement will be given precedence in which any of the aforementioned reasons of preference is found, for example, that statement being in authoritative texts, or being the statement of Imam A'zam, or being from Zahir al-Riwayah, etc.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is from a work on the rules of issuing fatwa (Rasm al-Mufti). It discusses the principles (wujuh al-tarjeeh) for preferring one scholarly opinion over another in case of conflict. The author mentions four reasons: (1) Benefit for endowment (waqf) – though this is specific to endowment issues. (2) Suitability for the time – exemplified by the change in the requirement for witness tazkiyah from Imam Abu Hanifa's time to that of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), where lying became common, and also the permissibility of ijarah for teaching, which was initially impermissible but later allowed due to changing needs. (3) Strength of evidence – a general principle. (4) A new evidence clarifying a position. The passage then summarizes that these reasons apply when two opinions are equally correct or when neither has been explicitly preferred, and the mufti should choose the one with any of these preferential factors, such as being in the authoritative texts, being from Imam Abu Hanifa, or being from Zahir al-Riwayah. This is a key rasm al-mufti principle for handling ikhtilaf in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
وجوہ ترجیح (wujuh al-tarjeeh): Reasons for preferring one ruling over another when there is scholarly conflict.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two prominent students of Imam Abu Hanifa.
تزکیہ (tazkiyah): The process of verifying the integrity of witnesses before their testimony is accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did scholars shift from the position of Imam Abu Hanifa to that of the Sahibayn on the issue of witness tazkiyah?
A) Because Sahibayn had stronger evidence from Quran
B) Because lying became widespread in society, making tazkiyah necessary
C) Because Imam Abu Hanifa changed his opinion later
D) Because the endowment benefit required it

Key Takeaway
Preference among conflicting rulings in Hanafi fatwa is based on reasons such as benefit, suitability for time, strength of evidence, and new evidence, allowing the mufti to choose the most fitting opinion.

Mafhum Muwafiq and Mafhum Mukhalif: Types and Application
Explaining types of implied meaning (mafhum) and their legal validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish mafhum muwafiq from mafhum mukhalif, identify the five subtypes of mafhum mukhalif, and state the Hanafi position on mafhum al-laqab.

Core Idea
Mafhum muwafiq is accepted by all; mafhum mukhalif has five types, but Hanafis reject mafhum al-laqab.

A mufti must not only rely on explicit texts (mantuq) but also understand the implied meanings (mafhum) that texts convey. Classical Hanafi usul distinguishes two broad categories of mafhum: muwafiq (where the unmentioned case shares the ruling by a stronger reason) and mukhalif (where the unmentioned case takes the opposite ruling). This lesson breaks down these categories and their subtypes, which are essential tools for fatwa derivation.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish mantuq and maskut
First, identify the explicit statement (mantuq) and what is left unsaid (maskut). The rulings for the unsaid are derived through mafhum.
Remember: mantuq is directly stated; maskut is implied.
2
Define mafhum muwafiq
Mafhum muwafiq gives the same ruling to the unmentioned case as the mentioned case, based on language idiom without need for ijtihad. Example: 'Do not say uff' implies prohibition of beating by stronger reason.
This type is agreed upon by all schools.
3
Define mafhum mukhalif and list its five subtypes
Mafhum mukhalif gives the opposite ruling to the unmentioned case. The five subtypes are: mafhum al-sifah (description), mafhum al-shart (condition), mafhum al-ghayah (limit), mafhum al-adad (number), and mafhum al-laqab (proper noun).
Each subtype has a distinct linguistic trigger.
4
Analyze the Hanafi-Shafi'i disagreement on mafhum al-laqab
Shafi'is accept all subtypes except mafhum al-laqab. Hanafis also reject mafhum al-laqab, considering it based on weak indication (dalalat al-ins). Note the practical outcome: e.g., 'Fi al-ghanam zakah' does not negate zakat on other animals for Hanafis.
This disagreement is legitimate; both positions have evidence.

Source Text

واعمل بمفهوم روايات اتى ما لم يخالف لصريح ثبتا
ترجمہ: (68) اور آپ ان روایتیوں کے مفہوم پر عمل کریں جو وارد ہوئی ہیں ۔ جب تک وہ کسی صریح ثابت شدہ بات کے خلاف نہ ہو۔
مفہوم اور اس کے اقسام:
یہ بات جان لیں کہ مفہوم کی دو قسمیں ہیں:
(1) مفہوم موافق اور وہ یہ ہے کہ الفاظ مسکوت (غیر مذکور) کے لیے منطوق کے (مذکور) کا حکم ثابت ہونے پر دلالت کریں۔ کلام کو محض زبان کے محاورات کے اعتبار سے سمجھنے کی وجہ سے یعنی وہ دلالت کرنا غور و فکر اور رائے و اجتہاد پر موقوف نہ ہو جیسے لا تقل لهما ا (ماں باپ کو 'ہوں' بھی مت کہو) کی دلالت مارنے کی حرمت پر (اس کا دوسرا نام فحوى الخطاب ہے) (2) مفہوم مخالف : اور وہ یہ ہے کہ الفاظ مسکوت کے لیے منطوق کے حکم کی ضد کے ثابت ہونے پر دلالت کریں (اس کی بہت سی مثالیں اس کی اقسام کے ضمن میں آجائیں گی اور اس مفہوم کا دوسرا نام دلیل الخطاب ہے)

اور مفہوم مخالف کی متعدد اقسام ہیں (چند قسمیں درج ذیل ہیں) (1) مفہوم صفت : (اور وہ یہ ہے کہ کوئی حکم اسم صفت پر لگایا جائے تو جہاں وہ صفت نہ رہے گی حکم بھی نہ رہے گا) جیسے فی الشائمة زکوۃ (جنگل کی مباح گھاس چرنے والے چوپایوں میں زکوۃ ہے اس قول میں لفظ السائمۃ اسم مشتق ہے جو صفت پر دلالت کرتا ہے پس جو جانور سائمہ نہ ہوں گے بلکہ علوفہ ہوں گے ان میں زکوۃ نہ ہوگی)
(2) مفہوم شرط (اور وہ یہ ہے کہ کوئی حکم شرط کے ساتھ معلق کیا جائے تو جب شرط منفی ہوگی تو حکم بھی منتفی ہوگا) جیسے وإن كن أولات حمل فأنفقوا عليهن (اور اگر مطلقہ عورتیں حمل والی ہوں تو حمل پیدا ہونے تک ان پر خرچ کرو)
(3) مفہوم غایت: (اور وہ یہ ہے کہ حکم کی کوئی حد مقرر کی گئی ہو تو اس غایت پر حکم خود بخود ہی ہو جائے گا) جیسے حتى تنكح زوجا غيره (مطلقہ ثلاثہ شوہر کے لیے حرام ہے یہاں حتی تنكح تک کہ وہ اس (شوہر اول) کے علاوہ کسی اور شوہر سے نکاح کرے)
(4) مفہوم عدد: (اور وہ یہ ہے کہ حکم کی کوئی تعداد بیان کی گئی ہو تو وہ زائد کی نفی کرے گا) جیسے ثمانين جلدة (تہمت لگانے والوں کو اسی کوڑے مارو)
(5) مفہوم لقب : اور وہ یہ ہے کہ حکم کسی اسم جامد پر معلق کیا جائے جیسے في الغنم زكوة (بھیڑوں میں زکوۃ ہے) مفہوم کا حکم مفہوم کی دو قسموں میں سے پہلی قسم بالاتفاق معتبر ہے اور دوسری قسم میں مع اس کی تمام اقسام کے اختلاف ہے شوافع کے نزدیک آخری قسم (مفہوم لقب) کے علاوہ سب معتبر ہیں۔ ان کے نزدیک یہیں نص علوفه (گھر پر چارہ دئے جانے والے چوپایوں میں زکوۃ نہ ہونے پر دلالت کرتی ہے اور دوسری اس عورت کے لیے نفقہ نہ ہونے پر دلالت کرتی ہے جس کو طلاق بائنہ دی گئی ہو اور وہ حاملہ نہ ہو (اس کو متوتہ حائلہ کہتے ہیں) اور تیسری مطلقہ ثلاثہ کی حلت پر دلالت کرتی ہے جب کہ وہ کسی اور مرد سے نکاح کر لے (اور وہ جماع کے بعد طلاق دے دے یا مر جائے۔ یعنی حلت کے ثبوت کے لیے کسی اور نص کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اسی نص سے غایت کے بعد حلت ثابت ہوگی) اور چوتھی تہمت لگانے کی سزا میں اسی کوڑوں سے زائد کی نفی کرتی ہے۔
کیونکہ وہ دلالت انس سے استدلال ہے۔
And act upon the meaning of narrations that have come, as long as they do not contradict an established explicit text. Translation: (68) And you should act upon the meaning of these narrations that have been reported, as long as they are not contrary to any established explicit text.

Mafhum and its types:
Know that mafhum has two types:
(1) Mafhum muwafiq: it is that the words indicate the ruling for the unmentioned (maskut) being established similar to the mentioned (mantuq). This is because the speech is understood merely according to the idioms of the language, i.e., such indication does not depend on reflection and ijtihad. For example, 'Do not say 'uff' to them' indicates the prohibition of beating them. (Its other name is fahwa al-khitab.)
(2) Mafhum mukhalif: it is that the words indicate the opposite ruling for the unmentioned. (Many examples will come under its types. Its other name is dalil al-khitab.)

And mafhum mukhalif has many types (some types are as follows):
(1) Mafhum al-sifah: whenever a ruling is attached to a descriptive noun, then where that description is absent, the ruling is also absent. For example, 'In grazing livestock is zakat' – the word al-saimah is a derived noun indicating a description. So animals that are not grazing but are fodder-fed will have no zakat.
(2) Mafhum al-shart: whenever a ruling is suspended on a condition, then when the condition is negated, the ruling is also negated. For example, 'And if they are pregnant, then spend on them'.
(3) Mafhum al-ghayah: whenever a limit is set for a ruling, then at that limit the ruling automatically takes effect. For example, 'until she marries another husband' – the thrice-divorced woman is forbidden until she marries another husband.
(4) Mafhum al-adad: whenever a number is mentioned for a ruling, it negates any excess. For example, 'Eighty lashes'.
(5) Mafhum al-laqab: when a ruling is attached to a proper noun (ism jamid). For example, 'In goats is zakat.'
The ruling of mafhum: The first type (mafhum muwafiq) is considered valid by consensus. The second type (mafhum mukhalif) with all its types is subject to disagreement. According to the Shafi'is, all types except the last (mafhum al-laqab) are considered valid. According to them, the first text indicates no zakat on fodder-fed animals; the second indicates no maintenance for a woman divorced by final divorce who is not pregnant (called mutawata ha'il); the third indicates the permissibility of the thrice-divorced woman marrying another husband (after intercourse and divorce or death of the second husband, i.e., permissibility is established without need for another text); the fourth negates more than eighty lashes for the punishment of slander.
Because that is reasoning by indication of text?
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary on Rasm al-Mufti, deals with the concept of mafhum (implied meaning) in legal texts, a critical tool for the mufti. The author first divides mafhum into two categories: mafhum muwafiq and mafhum mukhalif. Mafhum muwafiq is where the unmentioned case is given the same ruling as the mentioned case due to language context, e.g., the verse 'Do not say 'uff' to them' implies the prohibition of beating parents by a stronger reason (fahwa al-khitab). This type is accepted by all scholars. Mafhum mukhalif is where the unmentioned case takes the opposite ruling, such as when a ruling is attached to a condition, description, limit, number, or noun. The author then lists five subtypes of mafhum mukhalif: mafhum al-sifah (description), mafhum al-shart (condition), mafhum al-ghayah (limit), mafhum al-adad (number), and mafhum al-laqab (proper noun). Examples are given from zakat, divorce, and hudud. The Hanafi position is to accept all these subtypes, while the Shafi'is accept all except mafhum al-laqab. The passage emphasizes that the mufti must understand these distinctions to correctly derive rulings from texts.

Key Terms
مفہوم (mafhum): Implied meaning derived from the text; what is understood from speech beyond the literal wording.
منطوق (mantuq): What is explicitly stated in the text.
مسکوت (maskut): What is not explicitly mentioned in the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of mafhum mukhalif is NOT considered a valid legal proof?
A) Mafhum al-sifah
B) Mafhum al-shart
C) Mafhum al-ghayah
D) Mafhum al-laqab

Key Takeaway
Mafhum muwafiq is universally accepted; mafhum mukhalif has five subtypes, of which mafhum al-laqab is not accepted by Hanafis, while the other four are valid proofs.

Mafhum al-Mukhalafa: Types, Hanafi Position, and Mufti's Application
Explains types of mafhum al-mukhalafa and the Hanafi position on its validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five types of mafhum al-mukhalafa, state the Hanafi rule that it is not valid in the primary texts of shari'ah, and apply this distinction when issuing fatwas.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-mukhalafa is not a proof in Quran and Hadith according to Hanafis, only in human speech and fiqh texts.

Mafhum al-mukhalafa (opposite implication) is a critical concept in usul al-fiqh that a mufti must handle with precision. The Hanafi school draws a sharp line: it is valid in everyday speech, transactions, and fiqh books, but not in the speech of the Lawgiver (Quran and Hadith). This lesson unpacks the five subtypes and the Shafi'i counterposition, equipping you to apply this rule when deriving rulings or evaluating evidences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five subtypes
List and define each type: mafhum al-sifah, al-shart, al-ghayah, al-adad, al-laqab. Use the examples given in the source to anchor your understanding.
2
Distinguish the two main categories
The source mentions 'the first of the two types' (mafhum al-muwafaqa) is agreed upon, while the second (mafhum al-mukhalafa) is disputed. Clarify which is which.
Mafhum al-muwafaqa is parallel implication; it is accepted by all.
3
Grasp the Hanafi position
Hanafis reject mafhum al-mukhalafa in the texts of shari'ah (Quran, Hadith) but accept it in human speech, transactions, and rational arguments. Note the evidence from Shams al-A'imma al-Kardari and the principle of dalalat al-ins.
4
Understand the Shafi'i position
Shafi'is accept all subtypes except mafhum al-laqab. They consider that specifying a description, condition, limit, or number implies negation of the ruling when that attribute is absent.
5
Apply the rule to fiqh texts and Companions' sayings
Mafhum al-mukhalafa is valid in fiqh 'ibarat and in Companions' statements based on ijtihad, but not in those that are marfu' (treat as hadith). Use the distinction from al-Nahr al-Fa'iq.
This is the practical takeaway for a mufti.

اور حنفیہ کے نزدیک صرف نصوص شرعیہ ( قرآن و حدیث ) میں دوسری قسم مع اس کی جملہ اقسام کے معتبر نہیں ہے اور اس مسئلہ کی مکمل تحقیق اصول فقہ کی کتابوں میں ہے۔ بول چال معاملات اور عقلیات میں مفہوم مخالف معتبر ہے تحریر کی شرح تقریر ( ج ا ص ۱۱۷) میں مصنف کے قول غیر معتبر فی کلام الشارع فقط کے بعد کہا ہے کہ شیخ جلال الدین خبازی (۱۱۵) نے ہدایہ کے حاشیہ میں شمس الائمہ کردری (۸۴) سے نقل کیا ہے کہ شارع کے ارشادات میں کسی چیز کا خصوصیت کے ساتھ تذکرہ اس کے ماسوا سے حکم کی نفی پر دلالت نہیں کرتا اور لوگوں کی باہمی گفتگو عرف معاملات اور دلائل عقلیہ میں دلالت کرتا ہے ( خبازی کی عبارت پوری ہوئی ) اور متاخرین نے اس بات کو ہاتھوں ہاتھ لیا ہے اور اس پر وہ مسئلہ متفرع معلوم ہوتا ہے جوخزانہ الامل اور خانیہ میں ہے کہ اگر کسی نے کہا کہ آپ کے میرے ذمہ سو درہم سے زیادہ نہیں ہے تو یہ سو کا اقرار ہو گیا۔ اور اس پر اس صورت میں کوئی چیز لازم نہ ہونے سے اشکال وارد نہیں ہوتا جبکہ کہا ہو کہ آپ کے میرے ذمہ سو درہم سے زیادہ بھی نہیں ہیں اور کم بھی نہیں ہیں جیسا کہ دونوں میں غور کرنے پر فرق پوشیدہ نہیں ہے۔ (التقریر کی عبارت پوری ہوئی )
عبارات فقہیہ اور اقوال صحابہ میں مفہوم مخالف معتبر ہے:
اور النہر الفائق کی کتاب الحج میں ہے کہ مفہوم مخالف روایات میں بالاتفاق معتبر ہے اور صحابہ کے ارشادات بھی اسی ذیل میں آتے ہیں، صاحب نہر نے فرمایا کہ اقوال صحابہ میں یہ قید بڑھانی مناسب ہے کہ : "وہ رائے واجتہاد سے جانے جا سکتے ہوں وہ اقوال مراد نہیں ہیں جو رائے واجتہاد سے نہیں جانے جا سکتے ۔" علامہ شامی رحمہ اللہ اس کی وضاحت کرتے ہیں کہ صحابہ کے ایسے ارشادات جو رائے و اجتہاد سے نہ جانے جا سکتے ہوں وہ حدیث مرفوع کے حکم میں ہیں، وہ نبی کریم ع کے ارشادات میں شامل ہیں اور احادیث میں مفہوم مخالف معتبر نہیں۔ پس صاحب نہر کی روایات" سے مراد وہ باتیں ہیں جو کتب فقہیہ میں مجتہدین سے مروی ہیں۔ خواہ وہ مجتہدین صحابہ کرام ہوں یا بعد کے حضرات اور النہر ہی میں سنن وضوء کے بیان میں ہے کہ " کتب فقہیہ میں مفہوم مخالف حجت ہے اور نصوص کے بیش تر مفہومات کا معاملہ اس سے مختلف ہے۔"
And mafhum al-mukhalafa has many types (some types are as follows): (1) Mafhum al-Sifah (implication of description): It is that a ruling is attached to a descriptive noun; when the description is not present, the ruling no longer exists. For example, 'Fi al-sa'imah zakah' (Zakah is due on livestock that graze in the wilderness). In this statement, the word 'al-sa'imah' is a derived noun indicating a description. So animals that are not grazing freely (i.e., are stall-fed) are not subject to zakah. (2) Mafhum al-Shart (implication of condition): It is that a ruling is suspended on a condition; when the condition is negated, the ruling is also negated. For example, 'And if they are pregnant, then spend on them' (regarding divorced women who are pregnant). (3) Mafhum al-Ghayah (implication of limit): It is that a limit is set for a ruling; upon reaching that limit, the ruling takes effect automatically. For example, 'until she marries another husband' regarding a woman divorced three times being unlawful for her first husband until she marries someone else. (4) Mafhum al-Adad (implication of number): It is that a number is specified for a ruling; it negates any greater number. For example, 'eighty lashes' for slanderers. (5) Mafhum al-Laqab (implication of title): It is that a ruling is attached to a non-derived noun (proper name). For example, 'Fi al-ghanam zakah' (Zakah is due on sheep). The ruling of mafhum: The first of the two types is accepted by consensus. The second type, along with all its subtypes, is disputed. According to the Shafi'is, all except the last type (mafhum al-laqab) are valid. For them, these texts indicate: the first indicates that stall-fed animals are not subject to zakah; the second indicates no maintenance for a woman given an irrevocable divorce who is not pregnant (called mutawwatih ha'il); the third indicates the permissibility (for the first husband) after she marries another man (and after consummation, divorces or dies); the fourth negates more than eighty lashes for slander. Because it is inference from implication (dalalat al-ins). According to the Hanafis, in the religious texts (Quran and Hadith) only, the second type and all its subtypes are not valid. A complete investigation of this issue is found in books of usul al-fiqh. In speech, transactions, and rational matters, mafhum al-mukhalafa is valid. In Sharh al-Taqrir of al-Tahrir (vol. 1, p. 117), after the author's statement 'invalid only in the speech of the Lawgiver', it is stated that Shaykh Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi (d. 115 AH) narrated from Shams al-A'imma al-Kardari (d. 84 AH) in his marginalia on al-Hidayah that: 'In the statements of the Lawgiver, specifically mentioning something does not negate the ruling from other than it. But in people's conversations, customary transactions, and rational proofs, it does indicate negation.' (End of Khabbazi's statement.) And the later scholars have accepted this enthusiastically. Upon this is based the issue found in Khizanah al-Amil and al-Khaniyah: if someone says, 'You do not have more than one hundred dirhams against me,' that is an acknowledgment of one hundred. No problem arises from the fact that something is not incumbent in the case when he says, 'You do not have more than one hundred dirhams and not less than one hundred,' because the difference is clear upon reflection. (End of al-Taqrir's statement.) Mafhum al-mukhalafa is valid in fiqh expressions (ibarat fiqhiyyah) and the sayings of the Companions. In al-Nahr al-Fa'iq, in the book of Hajj, it is stated that mafhum al-mukhalafa is valid by consensus in the transmitted reports (riwayat) and the statements of the Companions are included in this. The author of al-Nahr added the appropriate condition that these statements are those that can be known through opinion and ijtihad; not those that cannot be known through opinion and ijtihad. Imam Shami explains that those statements of the Companions that cannot be known through opinion and ijtihad are in the status of marfu' hadith; they are included in the statements of the Prophet, and mafhum al-mukhalafa is not valid in hadith. Therefore, by 'riwayat' al-Nahr means things transmitted in fiqh books from the mujtahids, whether they are Companions or later scholars. In al-Nahr itself, in the discussion of the Sunnahs of wudu, it is stated that 'In fiqh books, mafhum al-mukhalafa is a proof, but the matter of most mafhum in the texts (nusus) is different.'
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Rasm al-Mufti is a detailed discussion on mafhum al-mukhalafa (opposite implication) — a key concept in usul al-fiqh that a mufti must understand to issue proper fatwas. The author first enumerates five types of mafhum al-mukhalafa: mafhum al-sifah (implication of description), mafhum al-shart (implication of condition), mafhum al-ghayah (implication of limit), mafhum al-adad (implication of number), and mafhum al-laqab (implication of title). For each, he gives a definition and a Qur'anic or hadith example. He then states that the first type (mafhum mafhum — which refers to the first of the two main categories? Actually, the text says 'the first of the two types' meaning the type that is mafhum al-muwafaqa [parallel implication] as opposed to mafhum al-mukhalafa) is accepted by consensus. The second type (mafhum al-mukhalafa) is disputed. The Shafi'is accept all subtypes except mafhum al-laqab, while the Hanafis reject all subtypes of mafhum al-mukhalafa when applied to the primary texts of shari'ah (Qur'an and Sunnah). The Hanafi position is that mafhum al-mukhalafa is not valid in the speech of the Lawgiver (Quran and Hadith), but it is valid in everyday speech, customary transactions, and rational arguments. This is a crucial distinction: the mufti must not derive rulings from opposite implication when dealing with divine texts, but can use it in understanding people's statements and contracts. The passage then provides a practical example from fiqh works (Khizanah al-Amil, al-Khaniyah): if a person says 'You do not have more than one hundred dirhams against me,' it is considered an acknowledgment of exactly one hundred, based on mafhum al-mukhalafa (the opposite of 'more than' is 'equal to'). But if he says 'You do not have more than a hundred and not less than a hundred,' that is a different case. The passage then discusses the validity of mafhum al-mukhalafa in the expressions of fiqh books (ibarat fiqhiyyah) and the statements of the Companions. It notes that in fiqh books, mafhum is valid by consensus, but when it comes to the sayings of the Companions, a distinction is made: if the saying is based on opinion and ijtihad, mafhum is valid; if it is something that cannot be known through opinion (like matters of the unseen), then it is treated as marfu' hadith and mafhum al-mukhalafa does not apply. This teaches the mufti that the authority of a statement determines whether opposite implication can be used.

Key Terms
مفہوم مخالف (mafhum al-mukhalafa): The implied meaning opposite to the explicit wording; e.g., if a ruling is attached to a description, the implication is that the ruling is absent when the description is absent.
مفہوم صفت (mafhum al-sifah): Implication of description: a ruling attached to an adjective implies that the ruling changes when the adjective is absent.
مفہوم شرط (mafhum al-shart): Implication of condition: a ruling suspended on a condition implies its negation when the condition is absent.
مفہوم غایت (mafhum al-ghayah): Implication of limit: specifying an endpoint implies that the ruling changes beyond that point.
مفہوم عدد (mafhum al-adad): Implication of number: specifying a number implies that any greater number is not intended.
مفہوم لقب (mafhum al-laqab): Implication of a proper name or non-derived noun: e.g., 'in sheep is zakah' implies no zakah on other animals according to some.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which context is mafhum al-mukhalafa NOT considered a valid proof?
A) In everyday speech and transactions
B) In the primary texts of shari'ah (Quran and Hadith)
C) In the sayings of the Companions that are based on opinion and ijtihad
D) In fiqh books and juristic expressions

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti must never use mafhum al-mukhalafa to derive rulings from the Quran or Hadith; it is only valid in interpreting human speech and non-revelatory texts.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
12 min
Mafhum al-Mukhalafa in Hanafi Fatwa: Validity in Rational Arguments but Not in Primary Texts
Discusses validity of mafhum al-mukhalafa in legal reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction on mafhum al-mukhalafa to determine when a mufti may use it as evidence in fatwa, distinguishing between primary nusus and rational/fiqh reports.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-mukhalafa is invalid in Quran and Hadith but valid in rational arguments and juristic reports.

One of the most misunderstood tools in Hanafi usul is mafhum al-mukhalafa (opposite implication). Many students assume the Hanafi school rejects it entirely. This lesson clarifies that while Hanafis do not apply it to primary texts like the Quran and Hadith, they do accept it when reasoning from rational arguments (istidlal aqli) and from reports of juristic rulings (riwayat fiqhiyya). This nuanced position, refined by later scholars like Ibn Abidin, is critical for a mufti crafting fatwas from causes and conditions found in non-nass sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of statements discussed
The passage divides statements into: (a) primary nusus (Quran and Hadith, considered directly the Lawgiver's speech) and (b) rational arguments and juristic reports (e.g., statements of Companions, jurists' reasoning). The key is to recognize which category a given piece of evidence belongs to.
2
Apply the rule to each category
For nusus, the Hanafi rule is that specific mention does not negate other cases (mafhum al-mukhalafa is invalid). For rational arguments and fiqh reports, specific mention does indicate negation, so mafhum al-mukhalafa is valid.
3
Trace the proof from the examples
The passage uses two examples from al-Hidayah: (1) In ghusl, the word 'woman' is specific and implies the opposite for men. (2) Hadrat Umar's reasoning that 'initiation' (from his statement) implies the opposite: no initiation means no penalty. These are rational/fiqh examples, not primary texts.
4
Resolve the internal disagreement
The apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) and Fatawa Zahiriyya reject mafhum al-mukhalafa entirely. But later scholars (mutakhkhirin) like Imam Muhammad, al-Sarakhsi, al-Khassaf, and Ibn Abidin accept it for non-nass sources. The mufta bihi is the later view, which is relied upon for fatwa.

اور غایۃ البیان ہی میں باب جنایات انج میں جہاں صاحب ہدایہ نے یہ مسئلہ بیان کیا ہے کہ جب درندہ محرم پر حملہ کرے اور وہ اس کو قتل کر دے تو اس پر کوئی جزاء واجب نہیں ہے اس روایت کی وجہ سے جو حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہ سے مروی ہے کہ آپ نے ایک درندہ کوقتل کیا اور ایک مینڈھے کادم دیا اور ارشاد فرمایا کہ: "ہم نے ابتداء کی تھی (ہدایہ ج ص ۲۶۳) اس مسئلہ کی شرح کرتے ہوئے اتقانی (۴) نے لکھا ہے کہ: حضرت عمر نے دم دینے کی وجہ اپنی طرف سے ابتداء کرنے کو بیان کیا ہے اس سے یہ بات معلوم ہوئی کہ جب محرم نے قتل کرنے میں ابتداء نہ کی ہو بلکہ درندہ کے حملہ کو بنانے کے لیے اس کو قتل کیا ہو تو محرم پر کوئی جزاء واجب نہیں ہے ورنہ
شبه:
حضرت عمر کی بیان کی ہوئی وجہ کا کوئی فائدہ باقی نہ رہے گا ۔"
اور یہ نہ کہا جائے کہ کسی چیز کا خصوصیت کے ساتھ ذکر کرنا احناف کے نزدیک اس کے ماسوا سے حکم کی نفی پر دلالت نہیں کرتا، پھر حنفیہ حضرت عمر کے قول سے کیسے استدلال کرتے ہیں؟
جواب: اس لیے کہ میں کہوں گا کہ وہ قاعدہ شریعت کے ارشادات میں ہے رہی روایات اور استدلالات عقلیہ تو ان میں دلالت کرتا ہے اور حضرت عمر کا وجہ بیان کرنا استدلالات عقلیہ کے قبیل سے بنے (غایہ البیان کی عبارت پوری ہوئی ) اور مذکورہ بالا عبارت کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ احکام پر استدلال کبھی تو نص شرعی یعنی کسی آیت
یا حدیث سے کیا جاتا ہے۔ اور کبھی عقلی استدلال ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ حضرت عمر نے کیا ہے اور عقلی دلائل شارع کے کلام میں شمار نہیں ہیں اس لیے ان کا مفہوم مخالف معتبر ہو گا اور اسی وجہ سے فقہاء کہتے ہیں کہ : اس علت کا تقاضا فلاں بات کا جواز یا عدم جواز ہے، غرض وہ علتوں کے مفہوم مخالف سے استدلال کرتے ہیں۔
با ہمی گفتگو میں مفہوم مخالف معتبر ہونے پر اعتراض:
اب اگر آپ کہیں کہ الاشباہ کی کتاب القضا میں ہے کہ ” ظاہر روایت میں مفہوم مخالف سے استدلال لوگوں کے کلام میں جائز نہیں ہے جس طرح دلائل (نصوص) میں جائز نہیں ہے۔ رہا ( فقہی ) روایات کا مفہوم مخالف تو وہ حجت ہے جیسا کہ غایۃ البیان کی کتاب الحج میں

وہ بات جو فتاویٰ ظہیر یہ میں ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ مفہوم مخالف سے استدلال جائز نہیں اور یہی ہمارے علماء کی ظاہر روایت ہے اور وہ بات جس کو امام محمد نے سیر کبیر میں ذکر فرمایا ہے کہ مفہوم مخالف سے استدلال جائز ہے وہ بات ظاہر روایت کے خلاف ہے۔" کشف کے حواشی میں کہا ہے کہ میں نے فوائد ظہیر یہ کے باب مایکرہ فی الصلوۃ میں دیکھا ہے کہ مفہوم سے استدلال جائز ہے اس کو شمس الائمہ سری نے سیر کبیر میں ذکر کیا ہے اور فرمایا ہے کہ امام محمد نے سیر کبیر میں مفہوم مخالف سے استدلال کے جواز پر مسائل کی بنیاد رکھی ہے۔ اور امام خصاف رحمہ اللہ کا میلان بھی اسی طرف ہے اور انہوں نے کتاب الجیل میں
Start of the Rule of Drawing
And in Nay al-Bayan, where the author of al-Hidayah (vol. 3, p. 37) stated the ruling that in ghusl for janabah it is not obligatory for a woman to undo her braids, Qawam al-Din Amir's al-Itqani wrote: "By the word 'woman' avoidance of man is intended, and in fiqh reports, mentioning something specifically indicates by consensus the negation of what is other than it, contrary to the case of revealed texts (nusus), because in our view, in nusus, [specific mention] does not indicate the negation of what is other than it."
And in Ghayat al-Bayan itself, in the chapter of Jinayat [hunting violations], where the author of al-Hidayah stated the ruling that when a predatory animal attacks a pilgrim in ihram and he kills it, there is no penalty due upon him, because of the narration from Hadrat Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he killed a predatory animal and gave compensation of a ram, and said: "We had initiated [the attack]" (Hidayah vol. 3, p. 263). In explaining this ruling, al-Itqani wrote: "Hadrat Umar mentioned the reason for giving compensation as his own initiation. From this it is understood that if the pilgrim did not initiate the killing but rather killed the beast to repel its attack, then no penalty is due upon the pilgrim; otherwise, the wording 'Hadrat Umar said' would have no benefit."
And let it not be said that mentioning something specifically does not, according to the Hanafis, indicate negation of what is other than it; then how do the Hanafis use Hadrat Umar's statement as evidence?
Answer: Because I would say that that rule is in the statements of the Shari'ah; as for reports and rational arguments, [specific mention] does indicate negation in them, and Hadrat Umar's mention of the reason falls under rational arguments. (The text of Ghayat al-Bayan concludes.) And the gist of the aforementioned passage is that arguments for rulings are sometimes from a legal text (nass), meaning a verse or hadith, and sometimes rational arguments, as Hadrat Umar did. And rational proofs are not considered part of the words of the Lawgiver; therefore, their mafhum al-mukhalafa (opposite implication) is valid. For this reason, jurists say: "This cause requires such-and-such a ruling to be valid or invalid" — in short, they argue from the mafhum al-mukhalafa of causes.
Objection regarding the validity of mafhum al-mukhalafa in conversation:
Now if you say that in al-Ashbah, in the book of al-Qada, it says: "In the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), inferring from mafhum al-mukhalafa is not permissible in people's speech, just as it is not permissible in legal proofs (nusus). As for the mafhum al-mukhalafa of fiqh reports, it is a proof, as in Ghayat al-Bayan in the book of Hajj" (Hamawi, vol. 2, p. 336). Ibn Najim's statement contradicts what was previously mentioned, that mafhum al-mukhalafa is only invalid in the words of the Lawgiver.
Answer:
I (Allamah Shami) say that the view of the later scholars is what we previously mentioned: mafhum al-mukhalafa [is invalid] in the nusus of the Shari'ah. And Imam Muhammad and Allamah Biri (may Allah have mercy on him) wrote in Sharh al-Ashbah: "What is in Fatawa Zahiriyya is that inferring from mafhum al-mukhalafa is not permissible, and this is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) of our scholars. And what Imam Muhammad mentioned in al-Siyar al-Kabir, that inferring from mafhum al-mukhalafa is permissible, is contrary to the apparent narration." In the marginalia of Kashf, it is said: I saw in Fawaid Zahiriyya, in the chapter on what is disliked in prayer, that inferring from mafhum is permissible. Shams al-Aimma al-Sarakhsi mentioned that in al-Siyar al-Kabir and said that Imam Muhammad based rulings on the permissibility of inferring from mafhum al-mukhalafa in al-Siyar al-Kabir. And Imam al-Khassaf (may Allah have mercy on him) also inclined to this view, and he did so in Kitab al-Jayl.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage addresses a critical rule in Hanafi fatwa methodology: the validity of mafhum al-mukhalafa (opposite implication) as a tool for legal reasoning. The author begins by citing two examples from al-Hidayah where specific wording in fiqh reports (not primary texts) is used to infer the opposite ruling. He then clarifies that, according to the Hanafi school, mafhum al-mukhalafa is not valid when derived from the primary texts of the Quran and Sunna (nusus). However, when it comes to rational statements (istidlalat aqliyya) — such as a Companion's explanation for a ruling, as in the case of Hadrat Umar — mafhum al-mukhalafa is considered valid evidence. The reason is that rational arguments are not considered part of the Lawgiver's speech, so the principle that 'specific mention does not negate others' only applies to nusus. The passage then presents an objection based on a statement in al-Ashbah that mafhum al-mukhalafa is invalid in all types of speech. The response, attributed to Allamah Shami (Ibn Abidin), clarifies that the later relied-upon position distinguishes between nusus (where it is invalid) and rational arguments/fiqh reports (where it is valid). The passage also notes an internal disagreement: the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) — represented by Fatawa Zahiriyya — rejects mafhum al-mukhalafa entirely, but Imam Muhammad's view in al-Siyar al-Kabir accepts it, and this latter view is followed by many later scholars. Thus, a mufti must understand this nuanced hierarchy: for Quranic and hadith texts, mafhum al-mukhalafa is not used; for juristic reasoning and rational argumentation, it is a valid tool.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالف (mafhum al-mukhalafa): The opposite meaning inferred from a statement that specifies a condition, cause, or attribute, implying that the ruling does not apply to other cases.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The transmitted and well-known narrations within the Hanafi school, primarily from Imam Muhammad's six books, considered the authoritative source of rulings.
استدلال عقلي (istidlal aqli): Rational reasoning based on cause and effect, as opposed to textual revelation; in this passage, it is treated as a valid basis for using mafhum al-mukhalafa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi position as explained in this passage, in which type of statement is mafhum al-mukhalafa considered valid evidence?
A) In verses of the Quran
B) In hadith of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wasallam)
C) In rational arguments and fiqh reports
D) In all types of statements without exception

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa methodology, mafhum al-mukhalafa is a valid tool when derived from rational arguments or juristic reports, but not from primary revealed texts (Quran and Hadith).
