For more than a year and if the property is desert land, then renting it for more than three years is not permissible. Although both these matters are against the original school: in number 5 the original school is that guarantee is not obligatory, and in number 4 the original school is that no period is specified for ijarah. (7) The later scholars preventing the judge from deciding according to his knowledge. (8) The later scholars' fatwa that the husband cannot transfer his wife far away even if he has given her the entire prompt dower (cash); this fatwa is due to the corruption of the time. (9) The later scholars' fatwa that without testimony the husband's statement that after swearing an oath of divorce of his wife he said insha'Allah will not be accepted, although this fatwa is against the zahir al-riwaya, and the later scholars gave the reason for their fatwa as the corruption of the time. (10) The later scholars' fatwa that after love has occurred, the woman's statement that she did not receive that dower which was stipulated as a condition in the marriage will not be accepted, although the woman claims receipt of dower. And the rule of the school is: 'The claim of the one who claims receipt is believed, but the custom is that a woman does not surrender herself without receiving the prompt dower.' (11) And from the same category is the later scholars' statement that if the husband says 'Kullu hilli 'alayya haram' (every lawful thing is forbidden to me), then based on custom his wife will be divorced. The jurists of Balkh said that Imam Muhammad's statement 'Without intention divorce will not occur' was based on the custom of his region, and in our custom people intend by this statement to make the wife forbidden. Therefore it will be interpreted accordingly. This statement of the mashayikh of Balkh was transmitted by Allamah Qasim, and he transmitted from Mukhtarat al-Nawazil that the fatwa is upon this because the general usage in custom is this. Then Allamah Qasim said that in our region, the words used to make the wife forbidden include: (1) al-talaq yalzamuni (divorce is binding on me), (2) al-haramu yalwimu [yalzamu?] (the forbidden is binding on me), (3) 'alay al-talaq (upon me is divorce), (4) 'alayya al-haram (upon me is forbidden). (12) The father's claim that he did not make his daughter the owner of the dowry. The jurists also made this issue dependent on custom, although the rule is: 'Regarding making owner or not making owner, the statement of the one who makes owner is credible.' (13) Accepting the woman's statement regarding the deferred dower even though the statement of the one who denies is accepted. (14) The jurists' statement that in our time, due to necessity and general need, in muzara'ah, musaqat, and waqf, the opinion of the Sahibayn is preferred. (15) Imam Muhammad's directive that if the pre-emptor does not take action to become owner of the sold property for one month, his right of pre-emption is lost. Imam Muhammad said this to remove harm from the buyer. (16) And from the same category is the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad that if a free, sane, adult woman marries without a Kuf', the marriage is not valid. (17) And from the same category is the later scholars' fatwa due to necessity of overlooking the mud of the road. (18) And the fatwa of permissibility of bay' bi al-wafa. (19) The fatwa of permissibility of istisna' (ordering something to be made) (even though it is selling a non-existent thing). (20) The fatwa of permissibility of drinking water from a water carrier without specifying the quantity. Wafa' means to fulfill completely, and the form of bay' bi al-wafa is that a person needs money, he sells his property, land, house, etc., to someone, and between them it is agreed that when the seller returns the full amount, the buyer is bound to return the sale, i.e., he is bound to sell that thing to the seller at the original price. Since benefiting from usury was forbidden, people devised this stratagem. There was severe disagreement regarding the permissibility of bay' bi al-wafa. The scholars of Egypt generally considered it permissible. This issue is mentioned in Durr Mukhtar and Shami in the Book of Sales, Chapter of Exchange, and in Bahr in the Chapter of Option of Condition. Our elders did not give a fatwa of permissibility for this sale. 12
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage, from Sharh Rasm al-Mufti, lists numerous examples (numbered 4 to 20) of situations where later Hanafi scholars (muta'akhkhirin) issued fatwas that contradict the original positions recorded in the zahir al-riwaya of the school. The author explains the original ruling and then notes the later fatwa, often attributing the departure to fasad al-zaman (corruption of the time), 'urf (custom), or darurah (necessity). The passage illustrates a key principle of Hanafi ifta: a mufti may, under certain conditions, depart from the well-known position when the times change. For instance, (7) preventing a judge from using personal knowledge to decide, (8) not allowing a husband to move his wife far away even on payment of dower, (9) not accepting a husband's claim that he said insha'Allah after a divorce oath without evidence, (10) not accepting a wife's claim of non-receipt of dower once love is established, despite the rule that claimants are believed, because custom indicates otherwise. (11) Regarding expressive words like 'kullu hilli 'alayya haram', custom determines that it implies divorce. The mashayikh of Balkh reported that Imam Muhammad's ruling was based on their custom; in other places, the custom differs, so the fatwa changes. (12) A father's claim about not making his daughter owner of the jahiz is also left to custom. (13) Accepting the woman's claim about deferred mahr goes against the principle that the denier is believed. (14) Preference for the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) over Abu Hanifa in certain matters due to necessity and general affliction. (15) Imam Muhammad's view on shuf'ah (pre-emption) being lost after a month to protect the buyer. (16) The narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad that a woman marrying without a kuf' invalidates the marriage. (17) Overlooking mud on the road due to necessity. (18-20) Permissibility of bay' bi al-wafa (sale with repurchase), istisna' (manufacturing contract), and drinking water without specifying quantity. The passage ends with a definition of bay' bi al-wafa, noting disagreement and that Hanafi elders did not give fatwa on its permissibility. The numbering '12' at the end likely indicates the end of a section.

Key Terms
بیع بالوفاء (bay' bi al-wafa): A sale with the condition that the seller can repurchase the item at the same price when he returns the money, often used as a financing stratagem.
استصناع (istisna'): A contract to manufacture or construct something with advance payment, allowed despite involving a non-existent object at the time of contract.
ضرورت (darurah): Necessity that permits what is otherwise prohibited, but with strict limits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following statements best reflects the Hanafi elders' position on bay' bi al-wafa?
A) They permitted it due to necessity
B) They prohibited it absolutely
C) They did not give a fatwa on its permissibility
D) They considered it a valid sale like any other

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of bay' bi al-wafa and similar contracts is debated; the Hanafi elders did not permit it, showing that necessity has limits, especially in matters related to riba.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Mufti's Duty to Follow Custom ('Urf)
Establishing the mufti's duty to follow contemporary custom and the qualifications required.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of following contemporary custom when rulings were based on past custom, and identify the mufti's qualifications needed to distinguish valid from invalid custom.

Core Idea
A mufti must follow the new custom when the original ruling was based on a custom that has changed.

In this passage, the author establishes a key rule for the mufti: when a mujtahid has based a ruling on the custom of his time, and that custom has changed, the mufti must follow the new custom. The passage also emphasizes the mufti's need for insight and proper training to distinguish valid custom from invalid innovation. We will explore the conditions under which custom becomes a source for fatwa and why even a master of the books needs apprenticeship to learn the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
When a ruling is based on custom, the mufti follows the prevailing custom of his own time, not the custom of the mujtahid's time. This is because the ruling was implicitly tied to that custom.
This does not mean abandoning the madhhab; it means applying the underlying premise.
2
Understand the mufti's required qualifications
The mufti must have correct thinking, knowledge of Shariah rules, and the ability to discern valid custom (not contrary to Shariah) from invalid custom.
The early scholars required ijtihad; today at least competence in masail and conditions is needed.
3
Recognize the role of apprenticeship
Even if one memorizes all books of the imams, apprenticeship under an expert teacher is necessary to learn how custom influences fatwa in practice.
Quoted from Madinat al-Mufti: 'the path of giving fatwa becomes clear' through shagirdi.
4
Apply the rule from al-Qunyah
A mufti or judge should not rely solely on zahir al-riwayah while ignoring custom; ignoring custom can lead to injustice.
Al-Qunyah states it is not permissible to do so.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لہذا عرفی الفاظ میں مفتی نے عرف کی پیروی کرے گا اسی طرح ان احکام میں جن کا مدار مجتہد نے اپنے زمانہ کے عرف پر رکھا ہے اور وہ عرف بدل گیا ہے اور نیا عرف پیدا ہو گیا ہے تو مفتی انہیں حضرات کی پیروی میں نئے عرف کا اعتبار کرے گا۔
مفتی کا با بصیرت واقف عرف ہونا ضروری ہے: لیکن یہ ضروری ہے کہ مفتی ذی رائے ہو درست فکر رکھتا ہو اور شریعت کے قواعد سے واقف ہوتا کہ معتبر عرف جس پر احکام کا مدار رکھنا درست ہے۔ اور غیر معتبر عرف میں اختیار کر سکے کیونکہ متقدمین نے مفتی کے لیے اجتہاد کو شرط قرار دیا ہے اور یہ بات ہمارے زمانہ میں مفقود ہے اس لیے کم از کم کسی در خا تو ہونی ہی چاہیے کہ مفتی مسائل کو ان کی قیود و شروط کے ساتھ جانتا ہو کیونکہ فقہاء بار ہا شرائط و قیود چھوڑ دیتے ہیں اور فقہ کے طالب علم کی سمجھ پر اعتماد کرتے ہوئے اس کی تصریح نہیں کرتے ۔
اس طرح مفتی کے لیے ضروری ہے کہ وہ اپنے زمانہ کا عرف جانتا ہو اور اہل زمانہ کے احوال سے واقف ہو اور اس سلسلہ میں اس نے کسی ماہر استاذ کے پاس رہ کر واقفیت حاصل کی ہو اور اسی وجہ سے مدینہ المفتی کے آخر میں لکھا ہے کہ:
اگر کسی شخص کو ہمارے ائمہ کی تمام کتا میں حفظ ہوں تو بھی فتوی دینے کے لیے شاگردی ضروری ہے تا کہ فتوی دینے کی راہ اس کی سمجھ میں آئے اس لیے کہ بہت سے مسائل میں اہل زمانہ کی اس عادت کے مطابق جو شریعت کے خلاف نہیں ہے جواب دیا جاتا ہے۔"
اور قنیہ (۳۳) میں ہے کہ: نہ مفتی کے لیے جائز نہ قاضی کے لیے کہ وہ ظاہر روایت کے مطابق فیصلہ کرے اور عرف کو چھوڑ دے۔
فتویٰ میں مصلحت کا لحاظ ضروری ہے:
اور اس سے قریب وہ عبارت ہے جو اشباہ میں فتاوی بزاز یہ (۴۱) سے نقل کی گئی ہے کہ مفتی اس مصلحت کے مطابق فتوی دے جو اس کی سمجھ میں آئے اور میں نے ردالمختار باب القسامه ج ۵ ص ۴۵۰) میں لکھا ہے کہ اس صورت میں جبکہ ولی مقتول جس محلہ میں لاش ملی ہے اس محلہ والوں کے علاوہ کسی آدمی پر قتل کا دعوی کرے اور محلہ والوں میں سے دو گواہ پیش کرے تو امام اعظم کے نزدیک وہ گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک قبول کی جائے گی۔ اس مسئلہ کی تفصیل کرنے کے بعد تنبیہ کا عنوان قائم کر کے علامہ شامی رحمہ اللہ نے لکھا ہے کہ ) علامہ حموی نے علامہ مقدی کا یہ قول نقل کیا ہے کہ:
میں امام صاحب کے قول پر فتویٰ دینے سے ٹھیرا رہا اور میں نے اس قول کی اشاعت نہیں ہونے دی۔ کیونکہ اس قول پر ضرر عام مرتب ہوتا ہے اس لیے کہ جو سرکش آدمی یہ قول جانتا ہے وہ لوگوں کو ایسے محلہ میں قتل کرے گا جہاں اس محلہ والوں کے سوا کوئی اور موجود نہ ہو کیونکہ اسے اطمینان ہو گا کہ محلہ والوں کی شہادت تو اس کے خلاف قبول نہیں ہوگی۔ اس لیے میں نے کہا کہ صاحبین کے قول پر فتونی مناسب ہے خاص طور پر جب کہ احکام زمانہ کی تبدیلی کے ساتھ بدلتے ہیں ۔ " ( ردالمختار کی عبارت پوری ہوئی )
مفتی کے لیے لوگوں کے احوال کا جاننا ضروری ہے:
اور فتح القدیر کی کتاب الصوم باب ما يوجب القضاء والكفارة ( ج ۲ ص ۲۵۹) میں جہاں صاحب ہدایہ نے یہ مسئلہ بیان کیا ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص دانتوں کے درمیان پھنسا ہوا گوشت کھا لے تو اگر وہ تھوڑا ہے تو روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا اور زیادہ ہے تو روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا اور امام زفر فرماتے ہیں کہ دونوں صورتوں میں ٹوٹ جائے گا اور چنے کی مقدار تکیل و کثیر کے درمیان حد فاصل ہے اور اگر اس گوشت کو باہر نکالا اور ہاتھ میں لے لیا پھر کھا گیا تو اس کا روزہ ( بہر صورت) ٹوٹ جانا چاہیے ...... اور چنے کی مقدار میں امام ابو یوسف کے نزد یک قضا واجب ہے کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے اور امام زفر کے نزدیک کفارہ بھی واجب ہے امام
Therefore, in customary matters, the mufti will follow custom. Similarly, in those rulings which the mujtahid based on the custom of his time, and that custom has changed and a new custom has emerged, the mufti will follow the new custom in accordance with those authorities. It is necessary for the mufti to be insightful and familiar with custom: But it is essential that the mufti be a person of opinion, possess correct thinking, and be familiar with the rules of Shariah so that he can distinguish between valid custom upon which rulings can be based and invalid custom. Because the early scholars made ijtihad a condition for the mufti, and that is lacking in our time, therefore at least a certain level of capability is necessary so that the mufti knows the masail along with their restrictions and conditions, because the fuqaha often omit conditions and restrictions, relying on the understanding of the student of fiqh without clarifying them. Thus it is necessary for the mufti to know the custom of his time and be aware of the circumstances of the people of the time, and in this regard he should have gained familiarity by studying under an expert teacher. For this reason, it is written at the end of Madinat al-Mufti: 'If a person has memorized all the books of our imams, still for giving fatwa, apprenticeship is necessary so that the path of giving fatwa becomes clear to him, because in many masail, the answer is given according to the habit of the people of the time that is not contrary to Shariah.' And in al-Qunyah (33) it is stated: 'It is not permissible for a mufti nor for a judge to give a ruling according to zahir al-riwayah and leave aside custom.' Consideration of public interest in fatwa is necessary: And close to this is the statement quoted in al-Ashbah from Fatawa Bazaziyyah (41) that 'The mufti gives fatwa according to the public interest that he perceives.' And I have written in Radd al-Muhtar (Bab al-Qasamah, vol. 5, p. 450) that in the case where the guardian of the murdered person claims murder against someone other than the residents of the locality where the body was found, and he produces two witnesses from among the residents, then according to Imam al-Azam that testimony will not be accepted, but according to the Sahibayn it will be accepted. After detailing this issue, Allamah Shami (may Allah have mercy on him) set up a heading of 'Tanbih' and wrote that Allamah Hamawi quoted Allamah Maqdisi's statement: 'I refrained from giving fatwa according to Imam's opinion and did not publicize that opinion, because public harm results from that opinion. For a rebellious person who knows this opinion will kill people in a locality where no one else is present besides the residents, because he will be assured that the testimony of the residents will not be accepted against him. Therefore, I said that giving fatwa according to the opinion of the Sahibayn is appropriate, especially since rulings change with the change of times.' (End of Radd al-Muhtar's text). It is necessary for the mufti to be aware of people's circumstances: And in Fath al-Qadir (Kitab al-Sawm, Bab ma yujib al-qada' wa al-kafarah, vol. 2, p. 259), where the author of al-Hidayah has stated the issue: If a person eats meat stuck between his teeth, if it is little, the fast is not broken, if it is much, the fast is broken. Imam Zufar says both cases break the fast, and a chickpea's amount is the borderline between little and much. If the meat is taken out and held in the hand and then eaten, the fast must be broken (in any case)... Regarding a chickpea's amount, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, qada is obligatory, not kaffarah; according to Imam Zufar, kaffarah is also obligatory. Imam...
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti ruling addressing the mufti's relationship with custom ('urf) and public interest (maslahah). The author begins by establishing a foundational rule: when a mujtahid (such as Abu Hanifa or the Sahibayn) based a ruling on the custom of his time, and that custom has changed, the mufti should follow the new custom according to the approach of those imams. This is not a departure from the madhhab but an application of the principle that fatwa is given according to the time. The author then emphasizes that the mufti must be discerning ('ذو رائے') and know the rules of Shariah to distinguish valid custom from invalid. He acknowledges that the early scholars required ijtihad for a mufti, but since that is lacking in our time, at least a thorough knowledge of masail with their conditions is needed. The author quotes Madinat al-Mufti to stress that even memorizing all books is insufficient without apprenticeship under a teacher, because many answers depend on contemporary custom that is not against Shariah. Al-Qunyah further states that it is not permissible for a mufti or judge to rely solely on zahir al-riwayah while ignoring custom. The passage then shifts to maslahah, quoting al-Ashbah and Fatawa Bazaziyyah that the mufti gives fatwa according to the public interest he sees. The author provides a concrete example from Radd al-Muhtar: in a murder case where the victim's guardian brings witnesses from the same locality where the body was found, Imam Abu Hanifa rejects their testimony due to suspicion of partiality, while the Sahibayn accept it. Allamah Shami reports that later scholars refrained from giving fatwa on Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion because it would cause public harm (rebellious individuals could murder with impunity). Instead, they adopted the Sahibayn's view, especially since rulings change with time. This illustrates the principle that a mufti may choose a weaker opinion within the madhhab if the stronger one leads to widespread harm. Finally, the author mentions a fasting issue from Fath al-Qadir about eating food stuck between teeth, where the amount (little vs. much) matters, with different opinions among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the point is that the mufti must know people's circumstances and apply appropriate rulings.

Key Terms
عرف ('urf): The prevalent custom of the people in a given time and place that is not contrary to Shariah.
ظاہر الروایة (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known and transmitted rulings of the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), which are the primary basis for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does al-Qunyah say about the mufti and custom?
A) The mufti may ignore custom if he follows zahir al-riwayah.
B) It is not permissible for the mufti or judge to give a ruling according to zahir al-riwayah and leave aside custom.
C) The mufti should follow custom only if it is mentioned in the Quran.
D) Custom can never override a clear text from the madhhab.

Key Takeaway
The mufti must follow the valid custom of his time, especially when rulings were originally based on custom, and he must be trained to distinguish valid from invalid custom.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
10 min
The Mufti's Duty to Consider Public Interest (Maslahah)
Illustrating the mufti's duty to consider public interest through the murder case example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of maslahah to select between conflicting Hanafi opinions in fatwa, using the murder case example as a model.

Core Idea
The mufti may adopt a weaker opinion within the madhhab if the stronger opinion leads to widespread public harm.

In this section, the author discusses the mufti's duty to consider public interest (maslahah) when issuing fatwas. He quotes from al-Ashbah and Fatawa Bazaziyyah that the mufti gives fatwa according to the public interest he perceives. The author then provides a concrete example from Radd al-Muhtar: a murder case where Imam Abu Hanifa rejects the testimony of residents, but the Sahibayn accept it. Later scholars, including Maqdisi and Hamawi, chose the Sahibayn's opinion to prevent public harm, illustrating that rulings can change with the times.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general principle
The mufti gives fatwa according to the public interest he perceives, as quoted from al-Ashbah. This is not arbitrary but guided by Shariah objectives.
Maslahah is used for tarjih between opinions, not as a standalone source.
2
Study the murder case scenario
If a murder victim's guardian brings a claim against a non-resident and brings two witnesses from the same locality, Imam Abu Hanifa rejects the testimony due to tuhma (suspicion of partiality). The Sahibayn accept it.
The difference hinges on whether the witnesses are considered biased.
3
Analyze the reasoning of later scholars
Allamah Maqdisi refrained from giving fatwa on Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion because it would cause widespread harm: criminals could kill in localities with only residents present, knowing their testimony would not be accepted.
This is a classic application of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking means to evil).
4
Apply the principle of changing rulings
The passage concludes that rulings change with the change of times. Therefore, the mufti adopts the opinion that prevents harm, even if it is not the strongest in terms of evidence.
This is a key principle in Hanafi rasm al-mufti.
5
Derive the lesson for fatwa practice
When two opinions exist within the madhhab, the mufti may choose the one that best serves public interest, provided it is not contrary to clear nass.
The tarjih is done by the mufti based on his perception of maslahah.

اس طرح مفتی کے لیے ضروری ہے کہ وہ اپنے زمانہ کا عرف جانتا ہو اور اہل زمانہ کے احوال سے واقف ہو اور اس سلسلہ میں اس نے کسی ماہر استاذ کے پاس رہ کر واقفیت حاصل کی ہو اور اسی وجہ سے مدینہ المفتی کے آخر میں لکھا ہے کہ:

فتویٰ میں مصلحت کا لحاظ ضروری ہے:

Therefore, in customary matters, the mufti will follow custom. Similarly, in those rulings which the mujtahid based on the custom of his time, and that custom has changed and a new custom has emerged, the mufti will follow the new custom in accordance with those authorities. It is necessary for the mufti to be insightful and familiar with custom: But it is essential that the mufti be a person of opinion, possess correct thinking, and be familiar with the rules of Shariah so that he can distinguish between valid custom upon which rulings can be based and invalid custom. Because the early scholars made ijtihad a condition for the mufti, and that is lacking in our time, therefore at least a certain level of capability is necessary so that the mufti knows the masail along with their restrictions and conditions, because the fuqaha often omit conditions and restrictions, relying on the understanding of the student of fiqh without clarifying them. Thus it is necessary for the mufti to know the custom of his time and be aware of the circumstances of the people of the time, and in this regard he should have gained familiarity by studying under an expert teacher. For this reason, it is written at the end of Madinat al-Mufti: 'If a person has memorized all the books of our imams, still for giving fatwa, apprenticeship is necessary so that the path of giving fatwa becomes clear to him, because in many masail, the answer is given according to the habit of the people of the time that is not contrary to Shariah.' And in al-Qunyah (33) it is stated: 'It is not permissible for a mufti nor for a judge to give a ruling according to zahir al-riwayah and leave aside custom.' Consideration of public interest in fatwa is necessary: And close to this is the statement quoted in al-Ashbah from Fatawa Bazaziyyah (41) that 'The mufti gives fatwa according to the public interest that he perceives.' And I have written in Radd al-Muhtar (Bab al-Qasamah, vol. 5, p. 450) that in the case where the guardian of the murdered person claims murder against someone other than the residents of the locality where the body was found, and he produces two witnesses from among the residents, then according to Imam al-Azam that testimony will not be accepted, but according to the Sahibayn it will be accepted. After detailing this issue, Allamah Shami (may Allah have mercy on him) set up a heading of 'Tanbih' and wrote that Allamah Hamawi quoted Allamah Maqdisi's statement: 'I refrained from giving fatwa according to Imam's opinion and did not publicize that opinion, because public harm results from that opinion. For a rebellious person who knows this opinion will kill people in a locality where no one else is present besides the residents, because he will be assured that the testimony of the residents will not be accepted against him. Therefore, I said that giving fatwa according to the opinion of the Sahibayn is appropriate, especially since rulings change with the change of times.' (End of Radd al-Muhtar's text). It is necessary for the mufti to be aware of people's circumstances: And in Fath al-Qadir (Kitab al-Sawm, Bab ma yujib al-qada' wa al-kafarah, vol. 2, p. 259), where the author of al-Hidayah has stated the issue: If a person eats meat stuck between his teeth, if it is little, the fast is not broken, if it is much, the fast is broken. Imam Zufar says both cases break the fast, and a chickpea's amount is the borderline between little and much. If the meat is taken out and held in the hand and then eaten, the fast must be broken (in any case)... Regarding a chickpea's amount, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, qada is obligatory, not kaffarah; according to Imam Zufar, kaffarah is also obligatory. Imam...
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti ruling addressing the mufti's relationship with custom ('urf) and public interest (maslahah). The author begins by establishing a foundational rule: when a mujtahid (such as Abu Hanifa or the Sahibayn) based a ruling on the custom of his time, and that custom has changed, the mufti should follow the new custom according to the approach of those imams. This is not a departure from the madhhab but an application of the principle that fatwa is given according to the time. The author then emphasizes that the mufti must be discerning ('ذو رائے') and know the rules of Shariah to distinguish valid custom from invalid. He acknowledges that the early scholars required ijtihad for a mufti, but since that is lacking in our time, at least a thorough knowledge of masail with their conditions is needed. The author quotes Madinat al-Mufti to stress that even memorizing all books is insufficient without apprenticeship under a teacher, because many answers depend on contemporary custom that is not against Shariah. Al-Qunyah further states that it is not permissible for a mufti or judge to rely solely on zahir al-riwayah while ignoring custom. The passage then shifts to maslahah, quoting al-Ashbah and Fatawa Bazaziyyah that the mufti gives fatwa according to the public interest he sees. The author provides a concrete example from Radd al-Muhtar: in a murder case where the victim's guardian brings witnesses from the same locality where the body was found, Imam Abu Hanifa rejects their testimony due to suspicion of partiality, while the Sahibayn accept it. Allamah Shami reports that later scholars refrained from giving fatwa on Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion because it would cause public harm (rebellious individuals could murder with impunity). Instead, they adopted the Sahibayn's view, especially since rulings change with time. This illustrates the principle that a mufti may choose a weaker opinion within the madhhab if the stronger one leads to widespread harm. Finally, the author mentions a fasting issue from Fath al-Qadir about eating food stuck between teeth, where the amount (little vs. much) matters, with different opinions among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the point is that the mufti must know people's circumstances and apply appropriate rulings.

Key Terms
مصلحت (maslahah): Public interest or benefit considered by the mufti when choosing between conflicting rulings, especially to avoid harm.
ضرر عام (darar 'amm): Widespread harm that affects the public. In this context, the harm that would result from applying Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Allamah Maqdisi refrain from giving fatwa on Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion in the murder case?
A) Because Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion was based on a weak hadith.
B) Because it would lead to widespread public harm, as criminals could exploit it.
C) Because the Sahibayn's opinion was easier to implement.
D) Because all scholars agreed that Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The mufti may adopt a weaker opinion within the madhhab when the stronger opinion leads to widespread harm, based on the principle that rulings can change with the times.

Mufti Must Follow Custom and Consider Maslahah
Beginning of Rasm al-Mufti with principle of following custom and maslahah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principles of 'urf and maslahah to choose between conflicting opinions in fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti must follow custom and consider public interest, even if it means departing from the stronger textual opinion.

This lesson introduces a foundational rule for muftis: fatwa must align with contemporary custom and consider public welfare. The author illustrates this with a qasamah case where Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is set aside by later scholars to prevent general harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two core principles
The passage states: a mufti will not give a fatwa contrary to the custom of his time, and consideration of maslahah is necessary. Recognize these as 'urf and maslahah.
These are not strict textual proofs but practical guidelines for fatwa.
2
Understand the qasamah dispute
In a case where only residents of the locality could testify, Imam Abu Hanifa rejected their testimony due to potential enmity, while the Sahibayn accepted it.
The dispute is over the reliability of witnesses who may be biased.
3
See how maslahah overrides the stronger opinion
Later scholars (e.g., Ibn Abidin) preferred the Sahibayn's opinion because Imam Abu Hanifa's view would cause general harm (darar 'amm) by encouraging criminals to kill in isolated places.
The stronger opinion (Imam Abu Hanifa) is abandoned to prevent widespread harm.
4
Note the application to change of times
The passage ends by noting that rulings change with the change of times, reinforcing the need for the mufti to consider contemporary circumstances.
Custom and maslahah are time-sensitive.

Beginning of Rasm al-Mufti: It is clear from what we have said earlier that a mufti will not give a fatwa contrary to the custom of his time. Consideration of maslahah in fatwa is necessary. And close to this is the passage that is quoted in al-Ashbah from Fatawa Bazaziyyah (41): The mufti gives fatwa according to the maslahah that he understands. And I wrote in Radd al-Mukhtar, book of Qasamah, vol. 5 p. 450, that in a case where the guardian of the murdered claims murder against someone other than the people of the locality where the corpse was found, and he produces two witnesses from the locality, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa that testimony will not be accepted, but according to the Sahibayn it will be accepted. So I said that giving fatwa according to the Sahibayn's opinion is appropriate, especially since rulings change with the change of times. (End of Radd al-Mukhtar's passage.)

Commentary
This passage opens the section on Rasm al-Mufti, establishing foundational rules for issuing fatwa. The author first states that a mufti must not contradict the custom of his time. Then he emphasizes that consideration of public interest (maslahah) is essential. He cites from Fatawa Bazaziyyah that the mufti should give fatwa according to the maslahah he perceives. To illustrate, he quotes Ibn Abidin's Radd al-Mukhtar: In a qasamah case where only the locality's residents could testify, Imam Abu Hanifa rejected their testimony due to enmity, but the Sahibayn accepted it. Later scholars preferred the Sahibayn's opinion to avoid general harm, showing that when a ruling leads to widespread harm, the mufti may choose the more beneficial opinion, especially as rulings evolve with changing circumstances.

Key Terms
عرف (urf): Customary practice of a particular time and place
مصلحت (maslahah): Public interest or benefit that justifies preferring one opinion over another

A mufti must align fatwa with contemporary custom and public interest, even if it means preferring a secondary opinion.

Custom in Fatwa: Only When Shari'ah-Compliant
Concluding statement emphasizing that lawful custom must be observed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi condition for valid custom ('urf) in fatwa, distinguishing between customs that are binding and those that are rejected.

Core Idea
Custom is binding in fatwa only if it does not contradict shari'ah.

This passage concludes a discussion on the role of custom ('urf) in issuing fatwa. The author reiterates the fundamental Hanafi principle: custom is considered in legal rulings, but only when it aligns with Islamic law. Examples of invalid customs include unjust taxes, octroi, and interest. This principle is essential for a mufti to navigate between societal practices and shari'ah boundaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal rule stated
Locate the core statement: that custom will be acted upon (urf par amal hoga) provided it is not contrary to shari'ah.
2
Recognize the condition (shart)
The condition is bishartike that the custom must not be khilaf shari'ah (contrary to Islamic law).
This condition distinguishes 'urf sahih from 'urf fasid.
3
Identify examples of invalid customs
The author lists taxes (tax), octroi (chungi), and interest (sūd) as customs that are contrary to shari'ah and thus not binding.
These are explicit examples of 'urf fasid.
4
Apply the rule to classify a custom
Given any custom, ask: does it involve something prohibited by shari'ah? If yes, it is invalid; if no, it is valid and binding.
5
Memorize the principle for fatwa practice
This rule is a foundational maxim (qa'ida) for a mufti: al-urf al-sahih mu'tabar, al-urf al-fasid ghayr mu'tabar.
Keep a mental checklist when encountering local customs in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This is the concluding paragraph that ties together the earlier discussions. The author reiterates the rule: custom ('urf) is given weight in fatwa, but only if it does not oppose Islamic law. He gives examples of unlawful customs: taxes (if unjust), octroi (a form of toll), and interest (riba). These are invalid despite being widespread. The passage underscores that not every custom is acceptable; it must pass the test of shari'ah compatibility. This principle is fundamental in Hanafi fiqh: 'urf sahih (valid custom) is considered, while 'urf fasid (corrupt custom) is rejected.

Key Terms
عرف (urf): Customary practice binding in fatwa if not against shari'ah
عرف صحیح (urf sahih): Valid custom that does not violate shari'ah
عرف فاسد (urf fasid): Invalid custom that contradicts shari'ah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Custom ('urf) is a valid source for fatwa only when it does not contradict shari'ah.

The Mufti's Criteria When Tarjih Is Absent
Rule for mufti when scholars differ without tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the three criteria (custom, ease, strong evidence) to select a ruling when scholars differ without tarjih, and identify when consultation is needed.

Core Idea
When tarjih is absent, the mufti weighs urf, ease, and dalil qawi — and consults an expert if he cannot distinguish.

A mufti often encounters scholarly opinions without clear preference. This Q&A from Tashih al-Quduri provides a concrete methodology: the mufti must consider custom, ease for people, strength of evidence, and current practice. If he cannot distinguish, he must consult a qualified scholar. This lesson unpacks that decision tree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the absence of tarjih
Recognize when the sources present multiple opinions without a clear preferred view (tarjih). This is the trigger for the mufti's independent selection process.
The question explicitly mentions scholars narrating without preference and disagreement on tashih.
2
Apply the three criteria
Evaluate each opinion against: (1) custom (urf) and changing conditions, (2) ease (narmi/rukhsah) for the people, (3) strength of evidence (dalil mazboot). Also consider what is in current practice (ta'amul).
These criteria are from the source: 'اعتبار کرے... اور اس قول کو لے جس میں لوگوں کے لیے نرمی ہے'
3
Determine if you can distinguish
Honestly assess your own ability to properly weigh the criteria and choose. The source says the world is never devoid of those who truly distinguish.
Self-deception (خود فریبی) is warned against.
4
Choose or refer
If confident, issue the fatwa using the selected opinion. If not, refer the questioner to a scholar who can distinguish. This fulfills your responsibility.
Referral is not a failure; it is part of the mufti's adab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک سوال: اور علامہ قاسم رحمہ اللہ کی تصحیح القدوری میں ہے کہ اگر کوئی پوچھے کہ علماء کبھی ترجیح دئے بغیر اقوال نقل کرتے ہیں اور کبھی ان حضرات میں تصحیح کے سلسلہ میں اختلاف ہو جاتا ہے تو ایسی صورت میں کیا کرنا چاہیے؟ جواب: تو میں جواب دوں گا کہ مفتی وہی کرے جو علماء کرتے ہیں یعنی عرف اور لوگوں کے احوال کی تبدیلی کا اعتبار کرے اور اس قول کو لے جس میں لوگوں کے لیے نرمی ہے اور جس پر تعامل جاری ہے اور جس کی دلیل مضبوط ہے اور دنیا کبھی ایسے لوگوں سے خالی نہیں ہوتی جو ان باتوں میں واقعی امتیاز کر سکتے ہیں، محض خود فریبی نہیں اور جو امتیاز نہیں کر سکتا وہ ان لوگوں کی طرف رجوع کرے جو امتیاز کر سکتے ہیں تا کہ وہ اپنی ذمہ داری سے عہدہ برآ ہو سکے ( علامہ قاسم کی عبارت پوری ہوئی )
A question: In Allamah Qasim's Tashih al-Quduri it is stated: If someone asks that sometimes scholars narrate opinions without preference, and sometimes there is disagreement among them regarding correction, what should be done in such a situation? Answer: I will answer that the mufti should do what the scholars do: consider custom and the change in people's conditions, and take the opinion that has ease for people, that is in current practice, and whose proof is strong. The world is never devoid of people who can truly distinguish in these matters, not just self-deception. And one who cannot distinguish should refer to those who can, so that he can fulfill his responsibility. (The passage from Allamah Qasim ends).
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This is a direct question-and-answer from the work Tashih al-Quduri by Allamah Qasim. The questioner is concerned about how to proceed when scholarly sources present multiple opinions without indicating which is preferred (tarjih) or when there is disagreement about which ruling is correct (tashih). The answer provides a clear methodology for the mufti: he should not arbitrarily pick an opinion. Instead, he considers three criteria: (1) custom (urf) and the changing conditions of people, (2) ease (rukhsah) for the people, (3) the strength of the evidence (dalil qawi). Additionally, he looks at what is practiced (ta'amul). If the mufti himself does not have the ability to distinguish (tamyiz) which opinion is most appropriate, he must consult those who do have that ability. This teaches that a mufti must be aware of his own limitations and seek guidance from more learned scholars to avoid issuing an incorrect fatwa.

Key Terms
تعامل (ta'amul): Established practice among people that is prevalent and accepted.
ترجیح (tarjih): Preferring one opinion over another based on evidence or other criteria.
تمییز (tamyiz): The ability to distinguish correctly between competing opinions based on sound reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the answer in Tashih al-Quduri, which of the following is NOT a criterion for the mufti to choose between conflicting opinions?
A) The custom (urf) and changing conditions of people.
B) The opinion that brings ease (narmi) to people.
C) The opinion most strongly supported by the rulers (hukkam).
D) The opinion that has strong evidence (dalil mazboot) and is in current practice (ta'amul).

Key Takeaway
When tarjih is absent, the mufti must weigh urf, ease, and strong evidence, consider ta'amul, and refer to capable scholars if he cannot distinguish.

Withholding a Fatwa to Prevent Oppression
Debating whether to give a technically correct fatwa that enables injustice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of sadd al-dhara'i to determine when a correct ruling should be withheld from fatwa due to anticipated misuse.

Core Idea
A correct ruling may be withheld from fatwa if its public dissemination enables oppression.

Imagine a correct fiqh ruling that, if made public, will be used by oppressive rulers to unjustly extract wealth from people. Should you still give it as a fatwa? This lesson explores a classical Hanafi debate where scholars intentionally withheld a ruling on land tax (kharaj) to prevent widespread injustice. You will learn how the principle of blocking the means to evil (sadd al-dhara'i) can override the general duty to convey knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Find the substantive fiqh ruling: if a landowner can grow a high-value crop but plants a low-value one, he is liable for the tax based on the high-value crop.
This ruling is technically correct in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Recognize the Harm
Understand the predicted harm: if this ruling becomes a public fatwa, oppressive rulers will claim any land could have grown high-value crops (e.g., saffron) and demand excessive taxes.
The harm is systemic injustice and usurpation of wealth.
3
Apply Sadd al-Dhara'i
Apply the principle of sadd al-dhara'i (blocking the means to evil) to justify withholding the fatwa. Although the ruling is correct, its dissemination creates a means to greater evil.
This principle is used by Hanafis and Malikis.
4
Resolve the Objection
Address the counterargument: 'How can you conceal a correct ruling?' The response: preventing greater harm (mafsadah) justifies this measure; the ruler's claim would often be false, leading to injustice.
The objection is dismissed by the higher priority of preventing harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور علماء نے یہ مسئلہ بیان کیا ہے کہ: 'اگر زمین والا اپنی زمین میں عمدہ چیز کی کاشت کی قدرت کے باوجود معمولی چیز ہوئے تو اس کے ذمہ اعلیٰ کاشت کا محصول واجب ہوگا۔' علماء نے فرمایا کہ یہ مسئلہ صرف جاننا چاہیے اس پر فتویٰ نہیں دینا چاہیے تا کہ ظالم حکام لوگوں کے اموال لینے میں بے باک نہ ہو جائیں۔ عنایہ شرح ہدایہ ( ج ۵ ص ۲۸۵) علی ہامش الفتح میں فرمایا ہے کہ اس بات کی یہ کہہ کر تردید کی گئی ہے کہ مسئلہ چھپانا کیسے جائز ہے؟ اور اگر ) حکام زائد محصول لیتے ہیں تو وہ لینے میں حق بجانب ہیں، کیونکہ وہ واجب ہے۔ اس تردید کا جواب یہ دیا گیا ہے کہ: اگر ہم یہ فتوی دیں گے تو ہر ظالم ایسی زمین کے بارے میں جو اعلیٰ درجہ کی نہیں ہے یہ دعویٰ کرے گا کہ اس میں پہلے مثال کے طور پر زعفران کی کاشت ہوتی تھی اور وہ اس کا محصول مانگے گا اور یہ ظلم و زیادتی ہے ۔ اھ اور فتح القدیر ( ج ۵ ص ۲۸۵) میں بھی ایسا ہی فرمایا ہے ۔ ابن الہمام لکھتے ہیں کہ: علماء نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس مسئلہ پر فتویٰ نہ دیا جائے کیونکہ یہ فتویٰ دینے کی صورت میں ظالم حکام مسلمانوں کے اموال پر مسلط ہو جائیں گے۔ ہر ظالم دعویٰ کرے گا کہ یہ زمین زعفران اور اس جیسی چیزوں کی کاشت کے قابل ہے اور اس کا علاج دشوار ہو گا ۔ اٹھے
And the scholars have stated this ruling: 'If the owner of land has the ability to cultivate a high-quality crop in his land but cultivates a low-quality crop, then he is liable for the tax of the high-quality cultivation.' The scholars said that this ruling should only be known (not taught publicly) and should not be given as a fatwa, so that oppressive rulers do not become emboldened in taking people's wealth. In al-Inayah commentary on al-Hidayah (vol. 5 p. 285) on the margin of al-Fath, it is stated that this was objected to by saying: How is it permissible to conceal a ruling? And if the rulers take additional tax, then they are justified in taking it because it is obligatory. The response to this objection is: If we give this fatwa, then every oppressor will claim about land that is not of high quality that previously, for example, saffron was cultivated on it, and he will demand its tax, and this is injustice and oppression. End. And similarly is stated in Fath al-Qadir (vol. 5 p. 285). Ibn al-Humam writes: Scholars have said that fatwa should not be given on this ruling because if it is given, oppressive rulers will overpower the wealth of Muslims. Every oppressor will claim that the land is suitable for saffron and similar crops, and its remedy will be difficult. End.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage addresses a delicate matter: when a theoretically correct fiqh ruling (that the landowner must pay tax based on the highest potential yield) is known to scholars but intentionally withheld from general fatwa. The reason given is pragmatic: if such a fatwa becomes public, oppressive rulers (zalamah hukkam) will use it to demand exorbitant taxes from farmers, claiming their land could have grown high-value crops like saffron, even if it never did. The text records an objection: how can we conceal a ruling of Shariah? The response is based on preventing greater harm (dar' al-mafasid): the fatwa would be exploited for injustice. Therefore, scholars deliberately restrict it to private knowledge among themselves. This is a classic example of considering the consequences (ma'alah al-af'al) in fatwa. The passage cites two major Hanafi works: al-Inayah (by al-Baberti) and Fath al-Qadir (by Ibn al-Humam) to support this position. It demonstrates that the mufti's duty includes protecting the public from foreseeable misuse of legal rulings.

Key Terms
محصول (mahsool): Land tax or revenue (kharaj) imposed on agricultural land.
سَدُّ الذَّرَائِع (sadd al-dhara'i): Blocking the means to evil; a principle used to prevent rulings that could be misused.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Hanafi scholars decide not to give fatwa on the ruling that a landowner must pay tax based on the highest potential crop?
A) Because the ruling itself is incorrect.
B) Because it would allow oppressive rulers to demand excessive taxes fraudulently.
C) Because the scholars did not know the actual ruling.
D) Because the landowners would protest.

Key Takeaway
The principle of sadd al-dhara'i can override the duty to publicize a ruling when doing so would cause greater harm.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
6 min
Weak Hadith Cannot Be Acted Upon in Fatwa
Stating the rule that weak hadith is not permissible to use in fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on using weak hadith in fatwa and identify the exception for darurah.

Core Idea
Weak hadith cannot be used in fatwa or judgment; only the rajih al-madhhab is relied upon.

This lesson presents a foundational rule from Rasm al-Mufti: weak hadith are not permissible for legal action or fatwa. The rule protects the integrity of Islamic law by ensuring that only reliable evidence is used. However, a narrow exception exists for scholars with necessity or deep knowledge, and judges are especially bound to follow the preponderant view of the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the default rule
Identify the core prohibition: weak hadith cannot be used as the basis for any action (fatwa, ruling, or practice).
The phrase 'لا يجوز بالضعيف العمل' is the primary hook for memorization.
2
Note the exception
Recognize the two exceptional cases: a scholar facing necessity (darurah) or one with well-known knowledge (ma'rifah mashhurah). In these cases, weak hadith may be used, but only under strict conditions.
These exceptions typically apply to fada'il al-a'mal (virtues of deeds), not to legal rulings (ahkam).
3
Apply the judge's restriction
Understand that judges must not rule by weak hadith. Their judgments are invalid if based on weak evidence. The judge's authority comes from following the rajih al-madhhab.
The phrase 'قضاتنا إذ قُدُوا براجح المذهب' emphasizes that Hanafi judges are trained to follow the strongest opinion.
4
Connect to fatwa hierarchy
Relate this rule to the hierarchy of evidence in fatwa: weak hadith is at the bottom; the mufti must prefer sahih/hasan hadith and established school positions.
This aligns with the principle that the mufta bihi is the rajih, not a da'if narration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ بِالصَّعِيفِ الْعَمَلُ ولا به يُجَابُ مَن جَاءَ يَسْأَلُ بِهِ إلا لِعَامِل لَهُ ضَرُورَةً أَو مَنْ لَهُ مَعْرِفَةٌ مَشْهُورَةً -۲- بكتُمَا الْقَاضِي بِهِ لَا يَقْضِى وَإِن قَضَا فَحُكْمُهُ لَا يَمُضِى لاسِيَّمَا قُضَاتُنَا إِذْ قُدُوا بِرَاجِحِ الْمَذْهَبِ حِيْنَ فَلِدُوا
Action upon weak (hadith) is not permissible, nor should a questioner be answered with it, except for a scholar who has a necessity or one who has well-known knowledge. Likewise, the judge should not judge by it, and if he judges, his judgment is not effective, especially our judges, for they are guided by the preponderant view of the school when they are born.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This is a poetic rule from Rasm al-Mufti. It establishes that weak hadith cannot be used as evidence for a fatwa or judicial ruling. The exception is for a scholar who faces a necessity (darurah) or who has well-established knowledge (ma'rifah mashhurah) – possibly referring to using weak hadith for fada'il al-a'mal (virtues of deeds). The second line emphasizes that judges must only rule by the preponderant (rajih) view of the Hanafi school, not by weak hadith. The phrase 'when they are born' is a metaphorical expression meaning that their training and orientation is to follow the strong views of the school.

Key Terms
صَعِيف (da'if): Weak hadith that does not meet the criteria for action in legal rulings
رَاجِحُ الْمَذْهَبِ (rajih al-madhhab): The preponderant or strongest opinion within the Hanafi school

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the poetic rule, what is the default position regarding a weak hadith in issuing fatwas?
A) It can be used if necessary.
B) It cannot be used at all except for one with necessity or well-known knowledge.
C) It is permissible if the mufti is knowledgeable.
D) It is acceptable for judicial rulings.

Key Takeaway
Weak hadith must not be used in fatwa or judgment; the mufti and judge are bound by the rajih al-madhhab.

Prohibition of Fatwa by Weak Opinions
Stating that weak opinions cannot be acted upon or used for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule prohibiting the use of weak opinions in fatwa and identify the two exceptions.

Core Idea
Only the preponderant (rajih) opinion may be used for fatwa; weak opinions are void unless necessity or expertise permits.

This lesson covers a cornerstone of Hanafi fatwa methodology: the rule that weak (da'if) and outweighed (marjuh) opinions are not to be acted upon or used to answer questions. The source is a poetic verse and commentary that clearly states the prohibition, its exceptions, and the binding nature of rajih opinions for judges. Understanding this rule is essential for any mufti to ensure fatwas conform to the madhhab's strongest evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The verse states unmistakably: لا يجوز بالضعيف العمل ولا به يجا (acting by weak opinion is not permissible and answering by it is not allowed).
This is the core prohibition.
2
Recognize the two exceptions
The text says إلا لعامل له ضرورة أو من له معرفة مشهورة (except for one in necessity or a highly knowledgeable expert).
These exceptions are precise and limited.
3
Understand the judge's position
The verse continues: القاضي به لا يقضي وإن قضى فحكمه لا يمضي (the judge does not judge by it; if he does, his judgment is unenforceable).
This emphasizes the binding nature of rajih opinions in judiciary.
4
Appreciate the commentary's reinforcement
The commentary cites Allamah Qasim that using a marjuh opinion is against consensus and that marjuh is null against rajih.
This reinforces the rule's authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ بِالصَّعِيفِ الْعَمَلُ ولا به يُجَابُ مَن جَاءَ يَسْأَلُ بِهِ ا إلا لِعَامِل لَهُ ضَرُورَةً أَو مَنْ لَهُ مَعْرِفَةٌ مَشْهُورَةً -۲- بكتُمَا الْقَاضِي بِهِ لَا يَقْضِى وَإِن قَضَا فَحُكُمُهُ لَا يَمُضِى لاسِيَّمَا قُضَاتُنَا إِذْ قُدُوا بِرَاجِحِ الْمَذْهَبِ حِيْنَ فَلِدُوا (۷۰) اور ضعیف قول پر عمل جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور نہ ضعیف قول سے جواب دیا جائے گا۔ اس کو جو مسئلہ پوچھنے آیا ہے۔ (۷۱) مگر وہ عمل کرنے والا مستثنی ہے جس کو مجبوری ہے۔ یا وہ مفتی جس کو مہارت تامہ حاصل ہے۔ (۷۲) البته قاضی ضعیف قول کے مطابق فیصلہ نہیں کرے گا۔ اور اگر کرے گا تو وہ فیصلہ نافذ نہیں ہوگا۔ (۷۳) خاص طور پر ہمارے زمانہ کے قاضی کیوں کہ وہ پابند کیے گئے ہیں۔ راجح مذہب کے مطابق فیصلہ کرنے کے جب ان کو عہدہ سونپا گیا ہے۔ (۷۴) اور پورے ہوئے وہ مضامین جو میں لڑی پر ور ہا تھا۔ اور الحمد للہ مشتک کی مہر ہے۔ ہم اس شرح کے آغاز میں علامہ قاسم رحمہ اللہ کے حوالہ سے بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ: (1) مرجوح قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کرنا یا فتوی دینا اجماع کے خلاف ہے۔ (۲) اور راجح قول کے مقابلہ میں مرجوح قول کالعدم ہے۔ (۳) اور متضاد روایات میں کسی مرجع کے بغیر ترجیح دینا ممنوع ہے۔ (۴) اور جو شخص بس اتنی بات پر اکتفاء کرتا ہے کہ اس کا فتویٰ یا اس کا عمل کسی بھی قول یا وجہ کے مطابق ہو جائے اور مختلف اقوال و وجوہ میں سے ترجیح میں غور و فکر کیے بغیر جس قول پر یا جس وجہ پر چاہتا ہے عمل کرتا ہے وہ یقیناً نادان ہے اور خرق اجتماع کرتا ہے۔ (علامہ قاسم کی باتوں کا خلاصہ پورا ہوا۔) اور پہلے وہیں ہم اسی طرح کی بات علامہ ابن حجر (۵) کے فتاوی کے حوالہ سے بھی بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
And it is not permissible to act by the weak (opinion), nor is it answered the one who comes asking by it, except for an actor who has necessity, or one who has well-known knowledge. (2) And likewise, the judge does not judge by it, and if he judges, his judgment does not pass (is not enforceable). Especially our judges, since they have been bound by the preponderant (rajih) of the madhhab when they were appointed. (Translation of verses: (70) And acting on a weak opinion is not permissible. And a weak opinion will not be used to answer the one who has come asking a question. (71) But the one who acts (by it) is exempted who is compelled, or a mufti who has complete expertise. (72) Of course, a judge will not decide according to a weak opinion. And if he does, that decision will not be enforceable. (73) Especially the judges of our time, because they are bound to decide according to the rajih of the madhhab when they were entrusted with the office. (74) And completed are the topics that I had strung in the poem. And praise be to Allah, the seal is musk. We have already mentioned at the beginning of this commentary, citing Allamah Qasim (may Allah have mercy on him) that: (1) To decide or give fatwa according to a marjuh opinion is against consensus. (2) And a marjuh opinion is null against a rajih opinion. (3) And to give preference among conflicting narrations without a source (of tarjih) is prohibited. (4) And the person who is content with just that his fatwa or his action agrees with any opinion or reason, and acts upon whichever opinion or reason he wants without reflecting on preference among the various opinions and reasons, is certainly ignorant and violates social cohesion. (The summary of Allamah Qasim's statements is complete.) And earlier there we mentioned the same from the Fatawa of Allamah Ibn Hajar (5).
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental rule of fatwa: only preponderant (rajih) opinions are to be acted upon and used for fatwa; weak (da'if) or outweighed (marjuh) opinions are not. The verses memorably state that acting on weak opinions is impermissible, giving fatwa by them is forbidden, and a judge who uses a weak opinion has his verdict unenforceable. Exceptions exist for necessity or an expert mufti who can properly gauge the weakness. The commentary adds that this rule is based on consensus, that marjuh is null against rajih, that arbitrary preference is prohibited, and that ignoring tarjih is ignorance and violates social harmony. This ties back to the mufti's duty to follow the madhhab's tarjih methodology.

Key Terms
ضعيف (da'if): A weak or less authentic opinion within the Hanafi school, typically one that is outweighed by stronger evidence.
مرجوح (marjuh): An opinion that has been outweighed (preponderated against) by a stronger (rajih) opinion.
راجح (rajih): The preponderant or stronger opinion in the madhhab, based on evidence and tarjih principles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what circumstances is it permissible to act by a weak (da'if) opinion?
A) Whenever the mufti prefers it
B) Only for a judge, not a mufti
C) For a person in necessity or an expert mufti with well-known knowledge
D) Never, under any circumstances

Key Takeaway
Weak opinions are not to be used for fatwa or judgment except in cases of genuine necessity or when the mufti is a renowned expert.

Acting upon Weak Opinions: Fatwa, Judgment, and Personal Practice
Explaining impermissibility of weak opinions with exceptions and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on acting upon weak (marjuh) opinions in fatwa, judgment, and personal practice, and explain the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
A mufti or judge must only use the preponderant (rajih) opinion; a weak (marjuh) opinion is void even for personal practice in the Hanafi school.

This lesson examines a foundational rule of ifta: a mufti must base his fatwa on the preponderant opinion (rajih) within the school. The source passage from a commentary on Rasm al-Mufti not only states the prohibition of using weak (marjuh) opinions but also delves into the exception for necessity and the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding personal practice. You will learn the precise limits of acting upon weak opinions.

1
Parse the poem verses (70-73)
Verses 70-73 are the core poetic statement.
2
Extract 'Allamah Qasim's four points
3
Analyze the dispute: Subki vs Shurunbulali
Note the metaphor of naskh is figurative.
4
Evaluate the objections and responses
5
Conclude the Hanafi position

وجوہ میں سے ترجیح میں غور و فکر کیے بغیر جس قول پر یا جس وجہ پر چاہتا ہے عمل کرتا ہے وہ یقیناً نادان ہے اور خرق اجتماع کرتا ہے۔ (علامہ قاسم کی باتوں کا خلاصہ پورا ہوا۔) اور پہلے وہیں ہم اسی طرح کی بات علامہ ابن حجر ( ۵ ) کے فتاوی کے حوالہ سے بھی بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ ضعیف قول پر عمل اور فتوی: لیکن علامہ کے فتاوی میں یہ بھی ہے کہ امام سبکی رحمہ اللہ (۱۱۶) نے اپنے فتاوی میں کتاب الوقف میں فرمایا ہے کہ: " نفس الامر میں ضعیف وجہ کی پیروی کرنا اپنے ذاتی عمل کے تعلق سے جائز ہے اور فتویٰ میں اور فیصلہ میں جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ علامہ ابن الصلاح ( ۷ ) نے اس کے عدم جواز پر اجماع نقل کیا ہے۔" اور علامہ شرنبلالی رحمہ اللہ (۴۶) نے اپنے رسالہ العِقْدُ الْفَريد في جَوازِ التقليد میں فرمایا ہے کہ: مذہب شافعی کا مقتضی جیسا کہ علامہ سبکی نے بیان کیا ہے۔ فیصلہ اور فتویٰ میں مرجوح قول پر عمل کا عدم جواز ہے اور اپنے ذاتی عمل کا یہ حکم نہیں ہے اور حنفیہ کا مذہب مرجوح قول پر عمل کا عدم جواز ہے اپنی ذات کے لیے بھی، کیونکہ مرجوح قول منسوخ ہو گیا ہے۔" شرنبلالی پر اعتراض: میں کہتا ہوں کہ عدم جواز کی یہ وجہ بیان کرنا کہ مرجوح قول منسوخ ہو گیا ہے صرف اس صورت میں معقول ہے جب کسی مسئلہ میں مجتہد کے دو قول ہوں اور اس نے ایک قول سے رجوع کر لیا ہو یا ایک قول کا دوسرے سے مؤخر ہونا معلوم ہواور نہ معقول نہیں ۔ مثلا کسی مسئلہ میں ایک قول امام ابو یوسف کا ہے اور دوسرا امام محمد کا تو اس میں نسخ کی کوئی صورت نہیں بنتی۔ جواب: لیکن علامہ شرنبلالی کی مراد یہ ہے کہ جب دو قولوں میں سے ایک قول کی تصحیح کی گئی ہو تو دوسرا قول بمنزلہ منسوخ ہو جائے گا ( حقیقی منسوخ ہونا ان کی مراد نہیں ہے ) اور علامہ قاسم کی اس بات کا مطلب بھی یہی ہے جو گزر چکی ہے کہ : " راجح قول کے مقابلہ میں مرجوح قول کالعدم ہے" علامہ سیکی پر اعتراض: پھر قول جیسا قول ہم اس شرح کے آغاز میں ابن حجر رحمہ اللہ کے فتاویٰ کے حوالہ سے بھی بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ انہوں نے اجماع نقل کیا ہے کہ آدمی جس
And completed what I composed in the string, and praise be to Allah, the seal of musk. Translation: (70) Acting upon a weak opinion is not permissible. And nor will an answer be given based on a weak opinion to the one who has come asking about a matter. (71) Except the one who acts is excused if he has a necessity, or the mufti who has complete expertise. (72) Certainly the judge will not give judgment according to a weak opinion. And if he does so, that judgment will not be enforceable. (73) Especially the judge of our time, because he is bound — when he was entrusted with the office — to give judgment according to the preponderant school. (74) And the topics I strung in a necklace are completed, and praise be to Allah, a seal of musk. The necklace was strung and Ahmad Shah... We have already mentioned at the beginning of this commentary, citing 'Allamah Qasim, that: (1) Giving judgment or issuing a fatwa according to a preponderate opinion is against consensus. (2) And in comparison to the preponderant opinion, the preponderate opinion is null and void. (3) And preferring among conflicting narrations without a criterion is prohibited. (4) And one who is content with the fact that his fatwa or his action conforms to any opinion or basis, and acts upon whichever opinion or basis he wishes without due consideration of preference among the various opinions and bases, is certainly ignorant and violates consensus. (Summary of 'Allamah Qasim's statements completed.) And previously there we also mentioned similar statements from the fatawa of 'Allamah Ibn Hajar. Acting upon a weak opinion and fatwa: But in 'Allamah's fatawa it is also that Imam Subki said in his fatawa in the chapter of Waqf: 'In reality, following a weak basis is permissible regarding one's personal practice, and not permissible in fatwa and judgment, because 'Allamah Ibn al-Salah narrated consensus on its impermissibility.' And 'Allamah Shurunbulali said in his treatise al-'Iqd al-Farid fi Jawaz al-Taqlid: 'The requirement of the Shafi'i school, as 'Allamah Subki stated, is the impermissibility of acting upon a preponderate opinion in judgment and fatwa, but that ruling does not apply to one's personal practice. And the Hanafi school holds the impermissibility of acting upon a preponderate opinion, even for oneself, because the preponderate opinion has become abrogated.' Objection on Shurunbulali: I say that stating this reason for impermissibility — that the preponderate opinion has become abrogated — is reasonable only when there are two opinions of a mujtahid on a matter and he has retracted one opinion, or the laterness of one opinion over the other is known; it is not reasonable otherwise. For example, in a matter one opinion is of Imam Abu Yusuf and the other of Imam Muhammad, there is no possibility of abrogation. Response: But 'Allamah Shurunbulali's intent is that when one of the two opinions has been rectified, the other opinion becomes like an abrogated one (he does not mean actual abrogation). And this is also the meaning of 'Allamah Qasim's earlier statement: 'In comparison to the preponderant opinion, the preponderate opinion is null and void.' Objection on Subki: Furthermore, what 'Allamah Subki mentioned — that according to Imam al-Shafi'i, acting upon a preponderate opinion regarding one's personal practice is permissible — contradicts what has passed citing 'Allamah Qasim, and a statement like that of 'Allamah Qasim we have also mentioned earlier in this commentary citing the fatawa of Ibn Hajar. Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on the poem 'Rasm al-Mufti'. It addresses a fundamental rule of ifta: a mufti must base his fatwa on the preponderant (rajih) opinion within his school, not on weak (marjuh) opinions. The poem verses 70-73 state: 1) Acting on or answering with a weak opinion is impermissible. 2) An exception is allowed for a person with a genuine necessity, or a mufti with complete expertise who may know the preferred view. 3) A judge cannot pass judgment based on a weak opinion; if he does, the judgment is not enforceable. 4) Especially in later times, judges are bound to the preponderant ruling of the school. Following this, the commentator summarizes from 'Allamah Qasim four key points: using marjuh in fatwa or judgment violates consensus; marjuh is null compared to rajih; preferring between conflicting reports without a criterion is prohibited; and one who randomly chooses any opinion without deliberation is ignorant and breaches consensus. Then, the discussion moves to a dispute: Imam Subki (Shafi'i) held that following a weak basis is permissible only for personal practice, not fatwa or judgment, citing the consensus of Ibn al-Salah. But 'Allamah Shurunbulali (Hanafi) asserts that in the Hanafi school, even personal practice on a marjuh opinion is forbidden because it is considered like abrogated (mansukh) — i.e., rendered obsolete by the existence of a stronger evidence. The commentator anticipates an objection: if two opinions come from different mujtahids (like Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), there is no abrogation of one by the other. He responds that Shurunbulali does not mean actual abrogation but that when one opinion is selected as the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, the other is treated as void. Further, the commentator notes an inconsistency: Subki's claim that Shafi'i allows personal practice contradicts the consensus reported by Qasim and Ibn Hajar that it is universally impermissible. This underscores that the Hanafi position is stricter — no personal practice on marjuh — and that the Shafi'i position is either misrepresented or an exception.

Key Terms
مرجوح قول (marjuh qawl): A legal opinion that is outweighed by stronger evidence and therefore not adopted as the relied-upon position.
ضعیف قول (da'if qawl): A weak opinion lacking strong evidentiary support; synonymous with marjuh in this context.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation; here used metaphorically to mean that a marjuh opinion is effectively abolished by the adoption of the rajih.
راجح (rajih): The preponderate or stronger opinion in a school, based on evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, is it permissible for a person to follow a weak (marjuh) opinion for his own personal practice?
A) Yes, it is permissible as long as it is not for giving fatwa or judgment.
B) No, it is not permissible, even for personal practice.
C) Yes, but only if the person has complete expertise (maharat tamah).
D) No, but only for matters of worship, not transactions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school strictly prohibits acting upon weak (marjuh) opinions in fatwa, judgment, and personal practice, with a narrow exception for genuine necessity.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
15 min
Ruling on Following Weak Opinions in Fatwa and Personal Practice
Discusses the rasm rule for following weak opinions and its exception for necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm rule regarding weak opinions to distinguish between permissible and impermissible use in fatwa, judgment, and personal practice.

Core Idea
A weak opinion is like null against the strong; it can only be followed in personal practice under necessity, never in fatwa or judgment.

This passage from a commentary on Rasm al-Mufti addresses a critical question for any mufti: can you act on a weak opinion yourself, or issue a fatwa based on it? The Hanafi school teaches that weak opinions lose legal force, but an exception exists for genuine necessity. Through careful analysis of objections and responses, the text clarifies the boundary between arbitrary desire and legitimate need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rasm rule
State the core rule: following a weak opinion in personal practice is permissible, but in fatwa and judgment it is not. Note the source of this rule in Ibn al-Salah's consensus.
This is the general principle before exceptions.
2
Compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions
Contrast the explicit Hanafi ruling (impermissible even personally, because weak is like abrogated) with the Shafi'i view (personal practice allowed). Understand the metaphor of abrogation as 'like non-existent' (ka'l-adam).
The Hanafi position is stricter in principle.
3
Analyze the objections and responses
Follow the two objections: one against Shurunbulali's abrogation argument and one against al-Subki's Shafi'i claim. See how the responses refine the rule: the abrogation is metaphorical, and the consensus against tashahhi (arbitrary selection) is not violated by necessity.
These objections reveal the nuance behind the rule.
4
Identify the exception of necessity
Recognize that necessity (darurah) permits following weak opinions even for personal practice, as shown by the examples of the traveler/guest and the ghusl/blood rulings. This exception is governed by the maxim 'al-darurah tubih al-mahzurat'.
Necessity is the key that unlocks the weak opinion.
5
Apply the rule to the furuat
Work through the two examples: (1) ghusl after nightmare following Abu Yusuf's opinion due to doubt, (2) blood from wound not nullifying wudu if not flowing. Confirm that in necessity, the weak opinion is acted upon, while the rajih opinion remains for fatwa and general practice.
These examples ground the abstract rule in real fiqh.
